GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 52.001 NET METERING.
   (A)   Findings. The findings and determinations set forth in the preambles
to the ordinance from which this section is derived are hereby made findings
and determinations of the Council.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 2, § 1)
   (B)   Encouraging investment. The town encourages interested citizens and
businesses to invest in renewable energy generation systems and enter in a net
metering arrangement with the municipal electric utility of the town.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 2, § 2)
   (C)   Eligibility. ELIGIBLE NET METERING CUSTOMERS include single-phase
customers in good standing that own and operate a renewable generating facility
that:
      (1)   Has a nameplate capacity less than or equal to ten kilowatts (kW);
      (2)   Is located on the customer’s premises and is operated by the
customer; and
      (3)   Is used primarily to offset all or part of the customer’s own
electricity requirements.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 2, § 3)
   (D)   Authorization of utility. The Council authorizes the utility to offer
net metering to eligible net metering customers on a first-come, first-serve
basis. The utility shall limit the aggregate amount of net metering facility
nameplate capacity from all eligible net metering customers to 0.1% of the
utility’s most recent summer peak load.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 2, § 4)
   (E)   Measurement of energy. The utility shall measure the difference
between the amount of energy delivered by the utility to the eligible net
metering customer and the amount of energy generated by the eligible net
metering customer and delivered to the utility. If the eligible net metering
customer generates more energy than it consumes in a month, the customer shall
receive a bill credit from the utility for the amount of surplus energy
generated. The utility shall not purchase or wheel power energy produced by an
eligible net metering customer’s facilities.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 2, § 5)
   (F)   Net metering tariff. The net metering tariff attached to the ordinance
from which this section is derived shall be adopted as the rates, terms, and
conditions under which the utility will offer net metering to eligible net
metering customers.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 2, § 6)
   (G)   Interconnection agreement. In accordance with the terms of the net
metering tariff, the utility shall enter into an interconnection agreement with
the eligible net metering customer, which incorporates technical
interconnection requirements and does not conflict with this section before the
net metering facility may be connected with the utility’s system.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 2, § 7)
   (H)   Unlawful connections. It shall be unlawful for any person or entity to
connect or maintain the connection of a renewable generating facility to the
utility’s system without first executing an interconnection agreement with the
utility.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 2, § 8)
(Ord. 2015-8, passed 12-1-2015) Penalty, see §
52.999
RULES AND REGULATIONS
§ 52.015 ADOPTION.
   The Town Council shall from time to time adopt such rules and regulations as
required for the operation of the municipal electric utility.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7A)
§ 52.016 RULES AND REGULATIONS ON FILE.
   A copy of all rates, rules, and regulations under which electric service
will be supplied is posted or on file for the public’s benefit in the office of
the Town Clerk-Treasurer and with the Public Service Commission of the state.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C1)
§ 52.017 WRITTEN APPLICATION OR CONTRACT REQUIRED.
   A written application or contract properly executed, may be required from
customers, before the town will be required to supply service provided,
however, that the town shall have the right to reject, for any valid reason,
any application. The town may require contracts for a long period of time when
unusual construction or equipment expense is necessary to furnish the service.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C2)
§ 52.018 DESCRIPTION OF ENERGY OR CURRENT TO BE FURNISHED.
   The customer shall, upon request of the town, present in writing to the town
a list of the devices which are to be attached to the town’s lines, giving the
location of the building, and the town will then advise the form, voltage, and
description of the current it will furnish.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C3)
§ 52.019 SERVICE CONNECTIONS.
   (A)   The town will locate the point to which service connection will be
brought to the building. The wires in the entrance run shall extend at least
three feet beyond the upper and outer end of the weatherproof fitting.
   (B)   (1)   Customer is responsible for following installation instruction
on Municipal L&P’s requirement sheet. For problems or questions, contact
Municipal L&P at 765-676-6331.
      (2)   Customer is responsible for making application for new service at
the Utility Billing Office located at 421 East Main Street. No meter will be
set until this requirement is fulfilled.
      (3)   Customer will contact Municipal L&P to schedule an onsite meeting.
All new or uprated services will need service locations approved whether
existing or proposed. If the customer desired new service attachment point not
acceptable to Municipal L&P, the Superintendent will at that time designate a
new point.
      (4)   Customer is responsible for building permits and for obtaining the
Building Inspector’s approval of the installation. After the installation of
the service by the customer the building inspector is to inspect each service
and indicate its approval. Additionally, Municipal L&P will make a final
inspection of the service up to the first point of disconnect to verify that it
is safe to hookup to the Municipal L&P system.
      (5)   The customer is responsible for meter bases, conduit up the utility
pole, and service wire to the first point of attachment only. All other
material will be supplied by the customer including trenching and backfilling
for the underground service, two and one-half inch conduit (including elbows)
as needed from the utility pole to the underground meter base, and all entrance
materials for overhead or underground services.
      (6)   The meter base will be mounted so that the center of the meter is
five feet six inches above final grade.
      (7)   Trenches for underground services must be inspected by Municipal
L&P prior to back filling to prevent possible problems. Trenches must be a
minimum of 36 inches deep to final grade and free of rocks and foreign objects.
Schedule 40 two and one-half inch PVC electrical conduit can be used below
grade but schedule 80 two and one-half inch PVC electrical conduit or rigid
metallic conduit must be used above grade. Conduit is required under driveways,
sidewalks, patios, and other places that may not be accessible after
installation.
      (8)   Riser pipes that Municipal L&P attaches to for overhead service
must be two-inch minimum rigid metallic conduit. If no attachment is to be made
on the riser, then rigid non-metallic (PVC) conduit may be used. The riser pipe
will be secured with approved clamps approximately three to four feet apart.
Two hole clamps are preferred because of their added holding capacity (no
service entrance cable allowed up to disconnect). The maximum attachment height
of the riser above the roof is 36-inch attachment heights greater than 36
inches require the use of a guyed support. Minimum height of the weatherhead
above the roof is 24 inches. Riser pipes through the roof must have roof
flashing approved for that use.
      (9)   An approved weatherhead must be used on all overhead installations.
Service entrance conductors at the weatherhead shall extend 18 inches to 24
inches out of the weatherhead and the neutral marked by stripping two inches
off of the insulation or marking tape.
      (10)   A five-inch by ten-foot or half-inch by ten-foot ground rod is to
be installed near the customer’s panel. The ground rod should be located out
from under the roof overhang in the most earth (approximately 18 inches). The
ground wire must be attached to the rod with approved brass or copper clamp.
The ground rod and wire are to be below grade to prevent damage or injury.
      (11)   If the fuse or breaker panel is not adjacent to the meter base the
customer may need to install an outside disconnect. When the installation of a
disconnect is required, the neutrals and grounds must be separated. Use of a
disconnect will also require the installation of a fourth wire from the
disconnect to the panel inside the dwelling. The need for the disconnect is the
responsibility of the Building Inspector.
      (12)   Conductor and ground wire sizing 100 amp #2 copper or #2 aluminum
grounding wire, #6 or #4 copper 200 amp #3/0 copper or #4/0 aluminum grounding
wire #4 copper.
      (13)   Interior wiring shall not be smaller than #12. All other wiring
shall be in accordance with the most current provisions of the National
Electric Code.
   (C)   The town will extend its lines a reasonable distance, as may be
determined by the town for the purpose of supplying electric service for a new
connection. Any changes made in service connections at the customer’s request,
after once installed, shall be at his or her expense.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C4) (Res. 94-2, passed 12-21-1994)
§ 52.020 INSIDE WIRING AND ENTRANCE EQUIPMENT.
   Applicants for service must, at their own expense, equip their premises with
all wiring, and entrance equipment, all of which shall be constructed and
maintained, subject to the approval of any authorized inspectors, and in
accordance with the rules and information of the town in force at the time. The
applicants shall at all times maintain the wires inside the building.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C5) Penalty, see
52.999
§ 52.021 LOCATION OF TOWN TRANSFORMERS, METERS, AND APPLIANCES.
   When the form of service requires, the customer shall provide free of
expense to the town, near service entrance, a suitable place for necessary
transformers, meter, or other appliances, which may be furnished by the town.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C6)
§ 52.022 METERS TO BE INSTALLED BY THE TOWN.
   (A)   (1)   The electricity, unless otherwise specified, shall be measured
by meter or meters of standard manufacture, installed by the town on the
premises in accordance with Rule 10 of Rules and Standards of Service for
Electrical Utilities, established by the Public Service Commission of the
state, effective May 1, 1920, Cause No. 5344, and the rules and information of
town in force at the time.
      (2)   Upon the registration of said meter or meters all bills, other than
the service charge, shall be calculated.
   (B)   (1)   If more than one meter is installed on different classes of
service, (each class being charged for at different rates), each meter shall be
considered by itself in calculating the amount of any bills.
      (2)   When, for the convenience of the town, more than one meter is
installed hereunder, on the same class of service, the sum of the registration
shall in all cases be taken as the total registration. Meters include all
measuring instruments.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C7)
§ 52.023 FAILURE OF METER.
   Whenever it is discovered that a meter is not recording correctly,
adjustment shall be made covering such inaccuracy in accordance with Rule 19 of
Rules and Standards of Service for Electrical Utilities as issued by Public
Service Commission the state, effective May 1, 1920, Cause 5344.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C8)
§ 52.024 BUILDING CONTAINING TWO OR MORE SEPARATE LIVING QUARTERS.
   (A)   Where service is supplied through one meter to a building containing
two or more separate living quarters, the customer shall, by written
application to the town, (on standard form prescribed by it for that purpose)
elect whether:
      (1)   The service shall be classed as residential, in residential rate
shall be multiplied by the number of occupied living quarters served through
the meter; or
      (2)   The service shall be classed as commercial, in which case, for
billing purposes, the commercial rate shall be applied on the basis of a single
customer.
   (B)   (1)   The election made by the customer shall continue for a period of
12 months and thereafter until the customer notifies the town, in writing, of
his or her election to have the selected classification of such service
changed.
      (2)   Each such election subsequent to the initial election shall
continue for a 12-month period and thereafter until the customer again notifies
the town, in writing, of his or her election to change his or her selection of
the classification of such service.
   (C)   (1)   The customer may arrange the wiring at his or her own expense,
so as to separate the combined service and permit the town to install a
separate meter for each separate living quarter.
      (2)   In each such case the readings of each such meter shall be billed
separately on the residential rate.
   (D)   This rule has no application to rooming houses.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C9)
§ 52.025 CONTINUED RESIDENTIAL AND COMMERCIAL SERVICE.
   (A)   Where both residential and commercial class of service are supplied
through one service and one meter to the same customer on the same premises,
such combined service shall be classed as commercial and billed under the
commercial service rate.
   (B)   At the option of the customer, the wiring may be so arranged at the
customers expense so as to separate the commercial service and residential
service to permit installations of two meters, in which case, the residential
rate will apply to the residential service and the commercial rate to the
commercial service.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C10)
§ 52.026 ACCESS TO PREMISES.
   The properly authorized agents of the town shall have the right to enter
upon the premises of the customer at all reasonable times for the purpose of
inspecting, repairing, or replacing all appliances used in connection with its
current, and removing the same on the termination of the contract or the
discontinuance of the service.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C11)
§ 52.027 CONTINUOUS SERVICE.
   The town shall not be responsible in damages for any failure to supply
electricity or for interruption, or reversal of the supply, if such failure,
interruption, or reversal is without willful default or negligence on its part.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C12)
§ 52.028 RELEASE OF TOWN FROM LIABILITY.
   The customer agrees that the town shall not be liable for damages resulting
to customer or to third persons from the use of electricity or the presence of
the town’s appliances, in the customer’s premises, unless due to willful
default or neglect on the part of the town.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C13)
§ 52.029 TOWN RESERVES RIGHT TO SHUT OFF SUPPLY.
   (A)   The town reserves the right to shut off the supply of electricity
without notice, for any of the following reasons:
      (1)   For repairs;
      (2)   For want of supply;
      (3)   For nonpayment of any bill when due;
      (4)   For interference with any of the town’s appliances or connections
thereto; or
      (5)   For failure to comply with the terms of the contract.
   (B)   Such discontinuance shall not, however, invalidate any contract, and
said town shall have the right to enforce any contract, notwithstanding such
discontinuance.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C14)
§ 52.030 DAMAGES.
   It is expressly stipulated by the town and agreed to by the customer, that
the town shall not be liable for damages because of any interruption to the
supply of current or for damages caused by defective wiring on the customer’s
premises.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C15)
§ 52.031 NOTIFY TOWN BEFORE INCREASING LOAD.
   The service connections, transformers, meters, and appliances supplied by
the town have definite capacity, and no substantial addition to the equipment
or connected load thereto will be allowed, except by written consent from the
town.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C16)
§ 52.032 MANNER IN WHICH CURRENT MAY BE USED.
   (A)   Electric current must be used for the purpose set forth in the
contract and in such a manner as not to cause unprovided for voltage
fluctuation.
   (B)   Lighting current must not be taken from power lines, nor current for
power purposes from lighting lines in excess of three horsepower, without the
consent of the town.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C18)
§ 52.033 RESALE OF CURRENT.
   The current furnished under the contract is for the use of the customers and
he or she shall not re-sell any of it or permit any person to use same without
written consent of the town.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C19)
§ 52.034 DEPOSIT.
   (A)   (1)   The town may require from all applicants for service a cash
deposit equal to the estimated consumption by such applicant for a period of 60
days as a guarantee against the nonpayment of bills for service; provided,
however, that, where consumer is the owner of property or furnishes a written
guarantee from a property owner, the town shall waive such cash deposit. Such
guarantee shall not make guarantor liable in an amount exceeding the charge for
a period of 60 days.
      (2)   Such cash deposit minus any unpaid amounts for service rendered
consumer shall be returned upon the discontinuance of service.
   (B)   In all cases, where the monthly consumption is in excess of that
covered by the deposit, the town may increase the amount of deposit required
but such deposit shall not exceed an amount for any estimated 60-day service.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C20) (Ord. 99-5, passed 3-2-1999)
§ 52.035 TOWN’S PROPERTY AND PROTECTION THEREOF.
   All meters, lamps or other appliances and equipment furnished by and at the
expense of the town, which may at any time be in said premises, shall, unless,
otherwise expressly provided herein, be and remain the property of the town,
and the customer shall protect such property from loss or damage, and no one
who is not an agent of the town shall be permitted to remove such property or
tamper therewith.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C21)
§ 52.036 EXCLUSIVE SERVICE ON INSTALLATION CONNECTED.
   No other electric light or power service shall, except under a contract for
auxiliary service, be used by the customer on the same installation in
conjunction with the town’s service, either by means of a “throw-over” switch
or any other connection.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C22) Penalty, see §
52.999
§ 52.037 MODIFICATION OF CONTRACT.
   No premises, agreements, or representations of any agent of the town shall
be binding upon the town unless the same shall have been incorporated in
contract in writing, before same is signed and approved.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C23)
§ 52.038 ASSIGNMENT.
   (A)   The benefits and obligations of any power agreement shall begin when
the town commences to supply electric service thereunder, and shall insure to
and be binding upon the successors and assigns, survivors and executors or
administrators, as the case may be, of the original parties hereto,
respectively, for the full terms hereof; provided that, no assignment hereof
shall be made by the customer without first obtaining the town’s written
consent.
   (B)   (1)   Lighting customers must make application to the office of the
town before they commence using the current.
      (2)   Lighting customers moving must notify the town in writing, or
otherwise they will be held responsible for the bills of their successors who
refuse to pay.
   (C)   No order for changing or discontinuing a contract will be accepted
over the telephone. All orders must be in writing.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C24)
§ 52.039 DELAY DUE TO STRIKES AND THE LIKE.
   Neither party shall be held liable for any failure or delay in performing
any of the things undertaken by it in this agreement in case such failure or
delay is caused by strikes, the act of God, or unavoidable accidents or
contingencies beyond its control and in no manner due to any fault, neglect, or
omission on its part.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C25)
§ 52.040 EQUIPMENT LOCATION PERMIT.
   The customer shall obtain and deliver to the town the necessary consent, on
the town’s forms, from property owner, or owners, to the installation and
maintenance in said premises and on, over, or through all private property of
all such wiring or other electrical equipment as may be necessary or convenient
for the supplying of electricity hereunder.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C26)
§ 52.041 MOTOR INSTALLATIONS.
   (A)   Motor installations of one or more motors aggregating five horse power
or less must be single phase unless three phase is available at the location
where the motor is to be used. Motor installations of one or more motors
aggregating 7-2’ horse power may be single phase, but should preferably be
three phase.
   (B)   Motor installations of one or more motors aggregating ten horse power
must be three phase, if three phase service is available.
   (C)   Motors of one-third horse power and under may be operated on lighting
circuits and may be wound for 110 or 220 volts. Single-phase motors in excess
of one-half horse power and up to three horse power, inclusive, must be wound
for 220 volts and can be connected on the 230 volt legs of the three wire
lighting service, but they must be run on a separate circuit.
   (D)   Single-phase motors in excess of three horse power individual capacity
must be covered by contract and must have a meter and power service outlet
separate and distinct from the meter and outlet for lighting service.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C27)
§ 52.042 MONTH.
   A MONTH means the period between any two consecutive regular readings by the
town of the meter or meters on the premises, such readings being taken as
nearly as practicable every 30 days.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C28)
§ 52.043 SHORT TIME SEASONABLE USE EACH YEAR OF POWER SERVICE.
   Where the nature of the business is seasonable (such as in canning factories
and the like) where service is used for a limited period regularly each year,
and the yearly minimum charge, or monthly minimum charge for each month for one
year, is not satisfactory to the customer, then the following rules will apply.
   (A)   In cases where the service line is in place and the customer has been
or is being served, the town will render service as provided for in the rate
schedule applicable to the type of service taken, provided that the customer
shall pay the cost of connecting and disconnecting the service in accordance
with the job work order procedure of the town. Only two connections and
disconnections shall be made in any one year under this rule, and the customer
is to make written application specifying the period or periods of service.
   (B)   The regular monthly minimum charge as provided for in the rate
schedule applicable to the type of service will apply for the period under
which service is taken.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C29)
§ 52.044 INSPECTIONS.
   The inspection of all such residences, business rooms, places of business,
and buildings shall conform to the National Electric Code of Rules, and shall
be made for the purpose of ascertaining the safety thereof and to protect the
said town against fire by reason of defective or unsafe or unsatisfactory
wiring.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 1, § 7C30)
RATES AND CHARGES
§ 52.055 ECONOMIC DEVELOPMENT RIDER.
   (A)   Findings. The findings and determinations set forth in the preambles
of the ordinance from which this section is derived are hereby made findings
and determinations of the Council.
   (B)   Adoption. The amended economic development rider attached to the
ordinance from this section is derived is hereby adopted by the Council, to be
effective immediately, replacing the current economic development rider.
   (C)   Economic development rider.
      (1)   Availability. This rider is available to a qualifying customer (as
defined herein) to encourage large power users to expand or create new
operations within the utility’s service territory.
      (2)   Qualifications.
         (a)   For the purpose of this section, the following definition
applies unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
            QUALIFYING CUSTOMER. A new or existing nonresidential customer in
the utility’s service territory that is establishing new operations or
expanding existing operations such that the new or expanded operations will
result in new or additional demand of at least one MW (1,000 kW) at one
delivery point (the “qualifying demand”) and the new or expanded operations has
involved a capital investment of at least $1,000,000 within the utility’s
service territory.
         (b)   For a qualifying customer that is expanding operations,
qualifying demand is measured from the average monthly peak demand for the 12
months immediately preceding the incentive period’s effective date. For a
qualifying customer that is establishing new operations, qualifying demand is
measured from zero.
         (c)   A qualifying customer is not a customer:
            1.   With “new” demand that results from a change in ownership of
an existing establishment without qualifying new load;
            2.   Renewing service following interruptions such as equipment
failure, temporary plant shutdown, strike, economic conditions, or natural
disaster; or
            3.   Has shifted its load from one operation or customer to another
within the utility’s service territory. The utility may determine exclusively,
without recourse by the customer, whether an event has occurred that would
prevent a customer from being a qualifying customer.
      (3)   Rate incentive. Beginning with the incentive period’s effective
date, utility will receive a credit on its wholesale bill for the qualifying
new load. The incentive amount received by utility from the Indiana Municipal
Power Agency for such load will be passed in full to qualifying customers. For
reference purposes, the discount to the qualifying customer’s wholesale cost
for qualifying new load will be calculated according to the following schedule:
 
Months 1-12  20%
Months 13-24 15%
Months 25-36 10%
Months 37-48 10%
Months 49-60 5%
 
         (a)   INCENTIVE PERIOD means months one through 60, as designated
above. The INCENTIVE PERIOD’S EFFECTIVE DATE means the first calendar day of
the first month in which the customer receives the incentive. If the incentive
period’s effective date is after December 31, 2023, the total incentive that
the qualifying customer may receive in each 12-month period shall be limited to
the incentive amount approved in the Indiana Municipal Power Agency’s Schedule
B in effect as of the incentive period’s effective date.
         (b)   The qualifying customer must meet the minimum qualifying demand
during each month of the incentive period. Failure to meet the minimum
qualifying demand in a particular month will result in 0% reduction for that
month.
      (4)   Terms and conditions.
         (a)   1.   The qualifying customer must submit a service application
to the utility specifying:
               a.   A description of the amount and nature of the new load;
               b.   The basis on which the qualifying customer meets the
requirements of this rider;
               c.   The qualifying customer’s desired effective date; and
               d.   Such other information as the member may require.
            2.   To receive the incentive, the qualifying customer will be
required to certify that one MW of connected new load has been added. Inactive
rider applications will expire at the earlier of either the termination of this
rider or one year from the application submission date. Customers may reapply
for the rider upon expiration of an application.
         (b)   This rider will terminate on the same date that IMPA’s economic
development rider terminates, except that any qualifying customer receiving the
rate incentive at the time of the rider’s termination may continue receiving
the incentive for the remainder of the applicable incentive period (as long as
it continues to meet the rider’s requirements).
      (5)   Applicable rate schedules. This rider is applicable to the rates in
this subchapter.
(Ord. 2023-05, passed 4-4-2023)
§ 52.056 ADOPTION OF RATES.
   (A)   The Phase 1 electric rates and charges set forth in §
52.062 and made a part hereof are hereby adopted and established for the use of
the service rendered by the Jamestown Power and Light, beginning July 1, 2022.
   (B)   The Phase 2 electric rates and charges set forth in §
52.063 and made a part hereof will replace the Phase 1 rates exactly one year
from the effective date of the Phase 1 rates and established for the use of the
service rendered by the town’s municipal electric utility.
   (C)   A purchase power adjustment set forth in §
52.064 and made a part hereof will be applicable with the rates established in
divisions (A) and (B) above.
   (D)   The utility’s non-recurring fees set forth in §
52.065 and made a part hereof will be applicable with the rates established in
divisions (A), (B), and (C) above.
   (E)   For the purpose of billing and collecting the charges for electric
use, the meters shall be read monthly, and the use shall be billed monthly.
   (F)   The electric utility rates and charges adopted hereby shall become
effective for all bills payable on or after July 1, 2022.
(Ord. 2022-03, passed 6-7-2022; Ord. 2023-05, passed 4-4-2023)

§ 52.058 PURCHASE POWER ADJUSTMENT.
   (A)   The purchase power adjustment (or tracker) factor is applicable to all
metered rates in dollars per kWh. It shall be calculated on the basis of a
factor occasioned solely by changes in the cost of purchased power and energy,
in accordance with the order of the State Utility Regulatory Commission,
approved on December 13, 1989, in Cause No. 36835-S3.
   (B)   The embedded base costs for the calculation of future purchase power
cost adjustment tracking factors are based on 2022 IMPA purchased power costs
as follows:
      (1)   Purchased power—demand: $24.834/kW-month; and
      (2)   Purchased power—energy: $0.030226/kWh.
   (C)   The purchase power adjustment is calculated quarterly and is expected
to vary depending on energy sales and purchase power charges. As a result,
customers can expect increases or decreases from quarter to quarter.
(Ord. 2022-03, passed 6-7-2022; Ord. 2023-05, passed 4-4-2023)
§ 52.059 NON-RECURRING CHARGES.
   (A)   Disconnect/reconnection charge.
      (1)   When service has been disconnected by the electric utility at the
facility’s option, a request to reconnect service during normal business hours
will require a reconnect charge of $50 prior to service being restored.
      (2)   The consumer, at his or her option, requests service to be restored
after normal business hours, as provided in division (A)(1) above, a charge of
$150 must be paid prior to reconnection.
   (B)   Insufficient funds. When a check that was received in payment of a
consumer’s account is returned unpaid by the bank for any reason (not the fault
of the electric utility), the consumer shall be assessed a handling charge of
$35 for each check returned by the bank.
   (C)   Consumer false callout. When a consumer calls the utility for service
restoration or repairs on the consumer’s premises and it is determined that the
problem is confined to the consumer’s property or facilities (such as a tripped
breaker, blown fuse, faulty wiring, and the like), a service charge of $50 may
be assessed toward the consumer’s account. The charge for this service after
business hours is $100.
   (D)   Damage to utility facilities. If a consumer causes damage to any
facility of the utility, the consumer shall be responsible for all costs
associated with repairing or replacing the damaged facilities.
(Ord. 2022-03, passed 6-7-2022; Ord. 2023-05, passed 4-4-2023)

   (A)   Availability. Available to any individual residential dwelling unit
for electric service used principally for residential purposes and served
through one meter when the maximum load requirements do not exceed 50
kilowatts.
   (B)   Character of service. Alternating current, 60 Hertz, at a voltage of
approximately 115 volts two-wire, or 115/230 volts three-wire, where available.
   (C)   Rate.

   (B)   Character of service. Alternating current, 60 Hertz, at a voltage of

§ 52.062 INDUSTRIAL POWER SERVICE RATE SCHEDULE.
   (A)   Availability of service. Availability to any customer whose maximum
load is 1,000 kVA or three-phase service is required. Customer must be located
adjacent to a distribution line having adequate capacity for the customer’s
requirements.
   (B)   Rate.
      (1)   Facility charge (per month) per kVA of connected transformer
capacity:
         (a)   Phase I: $1.35; and
         (b)   Phase II: $1.50.
      (2)   Distribution demand charge (per month in addition to facility
charge) per kW of metered monthly billing maximum load:
         (a)   Phase I: $2.12; and
         (b)   Phase II: $4.
   (C)   Billed demand and energy charges (subject to the provisions of §
52.063).
      (1)   The cost per kilowatt (kW) of billed demand shall be equal to the
current wholesale demand-related rate(s), including applicable demand
adjustment factors, of power purchased for the most recent month.
      (2)   The cost per kilowatt hour (kWh) of billed energy shall be equal to
the current wholesale energy-related rate(s), including applicable energy
adjustment factors, of power purchased for the most recent month.
   (D)   Reactive demand charge (subject to the provisions of §
52.063). The reactive demand charge shall be equal to the current wholesale
reactive demand rate of power purchased for the most recent month.
   (E)   Determination of billed demand and measurement of billed energy.
      (1)   The billed demand shall be measured by suitable recording
instruments provided by the utility, and in any month, the BILLED DEMAND shall
be the 60-minute integrated kW demand occurring in the same 60-minute interval
and on the same day of each month as the 60-minute integrated demand that will
be used by the Indiana Municipal Power Agency to bill the town.
      (2)   The billed demand shall be measured by suitable integrating
instruments and, in any month, the energy shall be the sum of the 60-minute
integrated kW demands.
   (F)   Determination of billing reactive demand. The billing reactive demand
for any billing period shall be the amount of reactive demand in kVARs by which
the metered reactive demand exceeds the reactive demand at a 97% power factor.
   (G)   Determination of distribution demand. Billing maximum load shall be
measured by suitable instruments and, in any month, the billing maximum load
shall be the average number of kW in the 30-minute interval during which the
demand metered is greater than that in any other 30-minute interval in such
month.
   (H)   Term of service. Service arrangements under Rate Schedule IP will be
made for an initial term of not less than one year with a longer term if
specified in a contract between the customer and the town.
   (I)   Special terms and conditions. Service under Rate Schedule IP normally
will be supplied through one metering installation. Where customer is served
from two or more delivery points to the same plant or location, the meter
readings may be totalized for the billing.
   (J)   Applicable wholesale rates.
      (1)   The cost per kilowatt (kW) of billed demand, billed energy, and
billed reactive demand shall be equal to the current wholesale rate(s),
including applicable demand adjustment factors, of power purchased the town:
         (a)   Billed demand charge: $24.834 per kW-month of billed demand;
         (b)   Billed reactive demand charge: $1.20 per kilovar-month (“kVAR”)
of excess billing reactive demand;
         (c)   Billed energy charge: $0.030632 per kWh-month;
         (d)   Demand ECA charge: $0.321 per kW-month of billed demand; and
         (e)   Energy ECA charge: $0.000406 per kWh-month.
      (2)   These rates are effective January through December 2022.
(Ord. 2022-03, passed 6-7-2022; Ord. 2023-05, passed 4-4-2023)

   (A)   Applicability. This section is applicable to §§

(Ord. 2022-03, passed 6-7-2022; Ord. 2023-05, passed 4-4-2023)
§ 52.067 BILLING AND DISCONNECT PROCEDURE.
   (A)   Bills for the rates and charges established by the town shall be sent
monthly. All bills shall be payable on the first day of the month following the
period of service and shall be paid at the office of the Clerk-Treasurer at 421
East Main Street, Jamestown, IN, during business hours or mailed to P.O. Box
165, Jamestown, IN 46147.
   (B)   If a bill is not paid by the fifteenth day of the month, it shall be
subject to the collection of a late payment charge and shall be added thereto
and collected therewith.
      (1)   Also, if bills are not paid by the fifteenth day of the month, a
written notice of discontinuance of service will be mailed to the customer and,
if not paid, the services will be disconnected 14 days after the town serves
notice upon the customer of its intent to terminate service or upon the twenty-
ninth day of the month, whichever occurs later, (if the fourteenth day after
the town serves notice upon the customer of its intent to terminate service or
the twenty-ninth day of the month, whichever is applicable, falls on a weekend
or a holiday the service will be disconnected on the following business day).
      (2)   The electric supply for the lot, parcel of land, or premises
affected shall be shut off and shall not be turned on again except on payment
in full of the delinquent bill, late payment charge, and reconnection charge.
(Ord. 2004-4, passed 10-5-2004; Ord. 2022-03, passed 6-7-2022; Ord. 2023-05,
passed 4-4-2023; Ord. 2024-05, passed 4-2-2024)
§ 52.068 RECONNECTION CHARGE/LATE CHARGES.
   (A)   When the electric service has been turned off by the electric utility
for the nonpayment of bill, the customer must pay a reconnection charge before
such service is reconnected at a rate of $50 during normal utility hours or
$150 outside normal utility hours.
   (B)   When a reconnection of service is made for a customer at the same
location more often than once in a 12-month period and service has, in each
case, been disconnected at the customer’s request, a charge of $50 may be made
by the utility for such reconnection of service during normal utility hours or
$150 if such reconnection is requested by the customer outside normal utility
hours.
   (C)   If a bill is not paid by the fifteenth day of the month, it shall be
subject to the collection of a late payment charge. Three percent of the amount
of the bill shall be added thereto and collected therewith.
(Ord. 2018-6, passed 7-3-2018; Ord. 2022-03, passed 6-7-2022; Ord. 2023-05,
passed 4-4-2023)
§ 52.069 TRACKING FACTOR.
   (A)   When future changes occur in the cost of purchased power which changes
would cause a change in said purchased power cost adjustment tracking factor
calculated in accordance with the order of the State Utility Regulatory
Commission approved on December 13, 1989, in Cause No. 36835-S3 as may be
thereafter amended by said Commission, such factor shall automatically be
changed accordingly.
   (B)   The embedded base costs for the calculation of future tracking factors
are based on 2022 IMPA purchased power costs as follows:
      (1)   Purchased power—demand: $24.834/kW-month; and
      (2)   Purchased power—energy: $0.030226/kWh.
   (C)   The tracking factor is calculated quarterly and is expected to vary
depending on energy sales and purchase power charges. As a result, customers
can expect increases or decreases from quarter to quarter.
(Ord. 96-1, passed 6-4-1996; Ord. 2022-03, passed 6-7-2022; Ord. 2023-05,
passed 4-4-2023)
§ 52.999 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Any person or entity found to be in violation of §
52.001 shall be fined not less than $500, nor more than $2,500 for each such
violation, plus costs. In addition to the foregoing fines, and at the utility’s
sole discretion, property where a renewable generating facility is unlawfully
connected to the utility’s system may be disconnected from the utility’s system
until an interconnection agreement is executed between the owner of such
property and the utility. Every day that a violation of this section occurs
shall constitute a separate offense.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 2, Ch. 2, § 8) (Ord. 2015-8, passed 12-1-2015)

RULES AND REGULATIONS
§ 53.01 BILLING PROCEDURE.
   (A)   (1)   Bills for the rates and charges established by the town shall be
sent monthly. All bills shall be payable on the first day of the month
following the period of service and shall be paid at the office of the Clerk-
Treasurer at 421 East Main Street, Jamestown, IN during business hours or
mailed to P.O. Box 165 Jamestown, IN 46147.
      (2)   If a bill is not paid by the fifteenth day of the month, it shall
be subject to the collection of a late payment charge and shall be added
thereto and collected therewith. Also, if bills are not paid by the fifteenth
day of the month, a written notice of discontinuance of service will be mailed
to the customer and, if not paid, the services will be disconnected 14 days
after the town serves notice upon the customer of its intent to terminate
service or upon the twenty-ninth day of the month, whichever occurs later, (if
the fourteenth day after the town serves notice upon the customer of its intent
to terminate service or the twenty-ninth day of the month, whichever is
applicable, falls on a weekend or a holiday, the service will be disconnected
on the following business day). The water supply for the lot, parcel of land,
or premises affected shall be shut off and shall not be turned on again except
on payment in full of the delinquent bill, late payment charge, and
reconnection charge.
   (B)   (1)   When the water service has been turned off by the water utility
for the nonpayment of bill, the customer must pay a reconnection charge of $20
before such service is reconnected.
      (2)   When a reconnection of service is made for a customer at the same
location more often than once in a 12-month period and service has, in each
case, been disconnected at the customer’s request, a charge of $20 may be made
by the utility for such reconnection of service.
      (3)   If a bill is not paid by the fifteenth day of the month, it shall
be subject to the collection of a late payment charge of 10% of the amount of
the bill shall be added thereto and collected therewith.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 2, § 1) (Ord. 2004-6, passed 10-5-2004 ;
Ord. 2024-05, passed 4-2- 2024)
§ 53.02 TAPPING FEES.
   (A)   Each user, at the time he or she is connected with the waterworks
system, shall pay a charge to cover the cost of tapping the main, furnishing
and laying service pipe, corporation and stop-cocks, service and meter box, and
installing the meter; provided, however, the tapping fee for three-quarter inch
service with five-eighths inch by three-quarter inch meter shall be $1,250 plus
all associated fees, plus state highway permit. In addition, all tap fees for
larger service shall be computed as set out below.
   (B)   (1)   All taps for water service in the mains of the waterworks system
shall be made under the direct authority and supervision of the Waterworks
Superintendent.
      (2)   All applications for a new water service shall be made in writing
to the Town Clerk- Treasurer or Superintendent and approved by the Town Council
before any taps are made.
   (C)   Subject to the limitations of this subchapter under §
53.06 regarding connection outside a frost proof hydrant, and §
53.12 regarding sale or transfer of ownership, any single-family addressed lot
located within the town’s corporate limits with more than one water meter
installed on or before October 4, 2022, is grandfathered and permitted to have
more than one meter so long as all tap fees and related fees have been paid for
each meter on or before November 6, 2022.
   (D)   For any meter installed on or before January 1, 2019, a presumption
arises that all tap fees and related fees have been paid, which presumption may
be rebutted with affirmative evidence that such tap fees and related fees were
not paid.
   (E)   After October 4, 2022, no additional user beyond those grandfathered
under division (C) above may have more than one water meter on any single-
family addressed lot located within the town’s corporate limits.
   (F)   No connection to the town’s waterworks system shall be allowed until a
payment of availability fees, tap fees, and all other related fees have been
made to the town.
(Ord. 96-5, passed 11-12-1996; Ord. 2002-6, passed 1-7-2003; Ord. 2004-6,
passed 10-5-2004; Ord. 2009-1, passed 3-3-2009; Ord. 2022-08, passed 10-4-2022)
Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.03 LARGER TAPS.
   Fees for any service larger than in §
53.02 shall be sufficient to cover the cost of tapping the main, finishing, and
laying service pipe, corporation and stop-cocks, service and meter box, and
installation of the meter.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 2, § 3)
§ 53.04 AVAILABILITY FEES.
   (A)   The charge to a user for a new connection to or additional water usage
from an existing connection to the town’s waterworks system and is charged as a
pro rata cost of construction of all water distribution mains and appurtenances
to serve the property of the connecting user and is charged in return for the
town making available to such user the town’s water supply system consisting of
all facilities and operations necessary to provide potable water to such user.
The amount of the availability fee shall be as follows:
      (1)   Residential user: $1,295 per EDU; and
      (2)   All other users: $1,295 per EDU.
   (B)   EQUIVALENT DWELLING UNIT (EDU) is defined as the average use of a
single-family dwelling over one calendar year. EDU determinations for water
users other than single-family dwellings shall be determined in accordance with
327 I.A.C. Article 8.
   (C)   Where a project charge or recoupment agreement charge has been
established prior to the date of this section, the project charge or recoupment
agreement charge shall apply. The cost of distribution systems constructed
after the date of this section by someone other than the town under a written
agreement with the town may be credited against the availability fee. The
decision to allow such credit, and the amount of the credit, shall be made
solely at the discretion of the town.

   (D)   Payment of the availability fee and tap fee shall be made at the

      (1)   For new construction connections or additional water usage from
existing water connections requiring plat or plan approval, one half of the

new construction added not requiring plat or plan approval, the availability
fee shall be paid in full before the additional usage is provided for the
town’s water system.

§ 53.05 TEMPORARY USERS.
   (A)   Water furnished to temporary users such as contractors, circuses, and
the like shall be charged on the basis of the metered gallon rates hereinbefore
set forth as estimated and established by the Waterworks Superintendent or the
Clerk-Treasurer.
   (B)   In case of temporary users such as contractors, street fairs,
carnivals, and the like, the Superintendent shall be authorized to demand
payment in advance for the amount of water estimated to be required.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 2, § 5)
§ 53.06 WATER METERS.
   (A)   All water meters shall be installed outside in tiles or inside
consumer’s premises (i.e., commercial/multi-family residence) in the location
and manner as selected by the Waterworks Superintendent. Any water only meter
located within the town’s corporate limits must be hooked up outside on a
frost-proof hydrant.
   (B)   Any refusal of prospective user to agree to meter location and/or
installation to serve best interest of town; or for a user grandfathered under
§
53.02(C) to have failed to pay all tap fees and related fees for any water
meter currently located on any single-family addressed lot located within the
town’s corporate limits on or before November 6, 2022, shall, at the option of
the Town Council, be sufficient reason to refuse water service until such
requirements are met.
(Ord. 2022-08, passed 10-4-2022)
§ 53.07 INSPECTIONS.
   A waterworks representative shall have the right to inspect at any
reasonable time all service piping and water appurtenances inside consumers’
premises.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 2, § 7)
§ 53.08 MULTIPLE CUSTOMERS.
   Any service pipe that supplies two or more customers shall be provided with
a separate stop-cock and separate meter for each customer, with minimum charge,
when consumption is minimum or under, applicable to each meter, except as
specified in §
53.13.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 2, § 8)
§ 53.09 SHUT OFFS.
   Water shall be turned off or on at curb cock or meter only by a waterworks
employee and not by customer. All service pipes must have stop and waste cocks
between outside meter and customer premises for emergency shut offs and making
of repairs.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 2, § 9)
§ 53.10 FIRE HYDRANT USE.
   No person shall take water from any fire hydrant except for fire purposes,
except upon the authority of the Superintendent.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 2, § 10) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.11 INTERFERENCE WITH UTILITY PROPERTY.
   All persons are forbidden to cover up or in any way interfere with any curb-
box, valve pit, valve box, or hydrant. In the case of any automobile or
vehicular accident involving the breaking or disconnection of a fire hydrant,
the car owner involved shall pay for the repair of same.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 2, § 11) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.12 PROHIBITED CONNECTIONS.
   (A)   Water customers shall not connect water service to any other property,
trailer, or customer without the written consent of the Town Council.
   (B)   Upon the sale or transfer of ownership of any single-family addressed
lot located within the town’s corporate limits occurring on or after October 4,
2022, any water-only meter located thereon shall be prohibited and subject to
disconnection.
(Ord. 2022-08, passed 10-4-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.13 DISCONNECTION.
   Water service to any customer may be discontinued for the following reasons:
   (A)   Wasting or improper use after same has been called to his or her
attention;
   (B)   Refusal to pay bills within prescribed time;
   (C)   For interfering with or destroying any water appurtenances or
appliances belonging to the town; and/or
   (D)   For connecting water service to any other property, trailer, or
consumer without proper authorization.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 2, § 13)
§ 53.14 AVERAGING BILLS.
   In case of failure of any meter, the town may bill consumption on the
average of billings for the last six months before meter failed to register
properly.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 2, § 14)
§ 53.15 DEPOSITS.
   (A)   The town may require from all applicants for service a cash deposit
equal to the estimated consumption by such applicant for a period of 60 days as
a guarantee against the nonpayment of bills for service; provided, however,
that, where the consumer is the owner of property or furnishes a written
guarantee from a property owner, the town shall waive such cash deposit. Such
guarantee shall not make guarantor liable in an amount exceeding the charge for
a period of 60 days. Such cash deposit minus any unpaid amounts for service
rendered consumers shall be returned upon the discontinuance of service.
   (B)   In all cases where the monthly consumption is in excess of that
covered by the deposit, the town may increase the amount of deposit required,
but such deposit shall not exceed an amount for any estimated 60-day service.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 2, § 15) (Ord. 99-5, passed 3-2-1999)
§ 53.16 SCHEDULE PUBLIC RECORD.
   A copy of the schedule of rates and charges and rules and regulations as
approved by the Town Council shall be on file and open to public inspection.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 2, § 16)
§ 53.17 EXTENSIONS.
   Main extensions to areas not previously served shall be made in conformity
to the “Rules and Standards of Service for Water Utilities” as approved by the
Public Service Commission of the state.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 2, § 17)
BACKFLOW REQUIREMENTS AND REGULATIONS
§ 53.30 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions apply unless
the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   CROSS-CONNECTION.
      (1)   Any physical connection or arrangement between two otherwise
separate systems, one of which contains potable water from the water system,
and the other contains water from a private source, water of unknown or
questionable safety, or steam, gases, or chemicals, whereby there may be a flow
from one system to the other, the direction of flow depending on the pressure
differential between the two systems.
      (2)   The utility is specifically a separate potable water system.
   UTILITY. The municipal drinking water system owned by the town, a
municipality and political subdivision of the state, and operated by its public
town water utility.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 3, § 1) (Ord. 2019-2, passed 3-5-2019)
§ 53.31 CROSS-CONNECTIONS PROHIBITED.
   (A)   No person shall establish or permit to be established or maintain or
permit to be maintained any cross-connection.
   (B)   No connection shall be established where potable water from a private,
auxiliary, or emergency water supply other than the regular public water supply
of the utility may enter the supply or distribution system of the utility,
unless such private, auxiliary, or emergency water supply and the method of
connection and use of such supply shall have been approved by the utility and
by the State Department of Environmental Management in accordance with 327
I.A.C. 8-10.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 3, § 2) (Ord. 2019-2, passed 3-5-2019)
Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.32 INSPECTIONS.
   The utility is hereby authorized to make inspections of any premises served
by the utility where a cross-connection with the utility is suspected or
possible. The frequency of inspections and re-inspections shall be established
by the utility in its discretion, based on the potential hazards involved.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 3, § 3) (Ord. 2019-2, passed 3-5-2019)
§ 53.33 RIGHT OF ENTRY.
   Pursuant to state law, including I.C. 36-1-6-2, and this subchapter, upon
presentation of credentials, authorized agents of the utility shall have the
right to enter at any reasonable time, real property served by the utility to
inspect for cross-connections. On request by the utility, the owner, lessee, or
occupant of any such premises shall furnish to the utility any pertinent
information about and access to the pipes, valves, drains, inlets, outlets, and
piping systems on the premises. The refusal of access or the refusal of
requested pertinent information shall be deemed evidence of the presence of
cross-connections on the premises.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 3, § 4) (Ord. 2019-2, passed 3-5-2019)
§ 53.34 DISCONTINUANCE OF WATER SERVICE.
   (A)   (1)   The utility is hereby authorized and directed to discontinue
water service to any premises wherein any connection in violation of this
subchapter exists, and a reasonable opportunity to correct the violation has
been given. The reasonableness of the opportunity to correct the violation is
fact-sensitive and will depend on the extent of the violation and the threat
posed to the public water supply. Water service to such property shall not be
restored until the cross-connection has been eliminated and the property is in
compliance with this subchapter.
      (2)   Water service shall be discontinued only after notice is served on
the owner, lessee, or occupants of the premises where a violation is found or
suspected to exist, and a reasonable opportunity to correct the violation has
been given. The reasonableness of the opportunity to correct the violation is
fact-sensitive and will depend on the extent of the violation and the threat
posed to the public water supply. Water service to such property shall not be
restored until the cross-connection has been eliminated and the property is in
compliance with this subchapter.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 3, § 5)
   (B)   (1)   If the utility, in its sole discretion, determines that a cross-
connection or emergency endangers public health, safety, or welfare and
requires immediate action, and a written finding to that effect is filed with
the Town Clerk-Treasurer and delivered to the consumer’s premises, then water
service to the premises may be immediately discontinued by the utility.
      (2)   Any person adversely affected by that discontinuance shall have the
opportunity to request a hearing within ten days of such emergency
discontinuance.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 3, § 6)
(Ord. 2019-2, passed 3-5-2019)
§ 53.35 REDUCED PRESSURE PRINCIPAL BACKFLOW PREVENTERS.
   (A)   All consumers using toxic or hazardous liquids and/or all hospitals,
mortuaries, wastewater treatment plants, laboratories, and all other hazardous
users shall install and maintain a reduced pressure principal backflow
preventer in the main water line serving each building on the premises. The
backflow preventer must be installed in an easily accessible location not
subject to flooding or freezing.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 3, § 7)
   (B)   Reduced pressure principal backflow preventers shall not be installed
below ground level.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 3, § 8)
(Ord. 2019-2, passed 3-5-2019) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.36 SUPPLEMENTARY TO STATE REGULATIONS.
   This subchapter does not supersede the State Plumbing Code, IDEM Rule 327
I.A.C. 8-10, or any other applicable building code, but is intended to be
supplementary to them.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 3, § 9) (Ord. 2019-2, passed 3-5-2019)
§ 53.37 BACKFLOW PREVENTION DEVICE.
   In addition to IDEM Rule 327 I.A.C. 8-10-4(c), from time to time, certain
specialized customer facilities will be required to install a backflow
prevention device, as determined by the utility and Council by amendment to
this subchapter.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 3, § 10) (Ord. 2019-2, passed 3-5-2019)
§ 53.38 NOTICE.
   If, in the judgment of the utility, an approved backflow prevention device
is necessary for the safety of the public water system, the utility shall give
notice to the water consumer to install such an approved device immediately.
The water consumer shall, at the customer’s own expense, promptly install such
an approved device at a location and in a manner approved by the utility and
shall have inspections and tests made of that device.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 3, § 11) (Ord. 2019-2, passed 3-5-2019)

   For use of any service rendered by the waterworks, each user shall be
charged in an amount based upon a fee schedule, shown in §
53.51.

§ 53.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   In addition to any other sanction provided by §§
53.30 through
53.38, a person who violates §§
53.30 through
53.38 shall, on the first offense, be fined $100. A person who violates §§
53.30 through
53.38 a second time will be fined the sum of $250. A person who violates §§
53.30 through
53.38 a third time, or more, shall be fined a sum not to exceed $2,500. The
foregoing shall be together with reasonable attorney’s fees incurred by the
town in enforcing §§
53.30 through
53.38.
(Prior Code, Title 5, Article 4, Ch. 3, § 12) (Ord. 2019-2, passed 3-5-2019)
