GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 71.01 TRAFFIC OVER PAVED STREETS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to drive or operate any tractor,
traction engine, wagon, truck, or other vehicle over, along, across, or upon
any street or alley in the town, which street or alley has been paved with any
asphalt or hard surface paving material, unless such tractor, Caterpillar
tractor, dredging machine, traction engine, wagon, truck, or other vehicle
shall be equipped with wheels having smooth treads; provided, however, that, if
any such tractor, Caterpillar tractor, dredging machine, traction engine,
wagon, truck, or other vehicle shall be equipped with wheels having flanged
treads or cleats, or other protuberances on such treads, such person or persons
may operate any such vehicle by driving same across any such street after
preparing and laying a tract or tracks for such vehicle designed to prevent the
treads of the wheels from coming in contact with such pavement.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 2) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.02 TRAFFIC WITHOUT WHEELS.
   Any such person desiring to cross any such street as aforesaid with any such
vehicle not being equipped with wheels having smooth treads shall first apply
to the Town Council for permission to do so, and such crossing shall be made
under the personal supervision and direction of the said Town Council.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 3) Penalty, see §
71.99
SNOW EMERGENCIES
§ 71.15 SHORT TITLE.
   This subchapter shall be known and be cited as the “Snow Emergency
Regulations and Routes.”
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 5, § 1)
§ 71.16 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions apply unless
the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ROADWAY. The portion of a street or highway designed or ordinarily used for
vehicular travel, exclusive of the berm or shoulder.
   SNOW EMERGENCY. A condition to be declared to be such by the Street
Commissioner upon the recommendation of the Police Department, or, in his or
her absence, his or her authorized representative.
   SNOW EMERGENCY ROUTE. Those streets or highways marked as such in accordance
with the provisions of this schedule.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 5, § 2)
§ 71.17 DECLARATION OF PARKING PROHIBITION ON SNOW EMERGENCY ROUTES.
   (A)   Whenever the Street Commissioner, upon the recommendation of the
Police Department, finds, on the basis of a falling snow, sleet, or freezing
rain, that weather conditions will make it necessary that motor traffic be
expedited and that parking on designated town streets be prohibited or
restricted for snow plowing and other purposes, the Street Commissioner shall
put into effect a parking prohibition on parts of, or all, snow emergency
routes as necessary by declaring it in a manner prescribed by this schedule.
   (B)   (1)   Once in effect, a prohibition under this subchapter shall remain
in effect until terminated by announcement of the Street Commissioner, upon
recommendation of the Police Department, in accordance with the provision of
this schedule; however, any street area which has become substantially clear of
snow and ice from curb to curb for the length of the entire block shall be
automatically excluded therefrom.
      (2)   While the prohibition is in effect, no person shall park or allow
to remain parked any vehicle on any portion of a snow emergency rote to which
it applies. However, nothing in this schedule shall be construed to permit
parking at any time or place where it is forbidden by any other provision of
law.
   (C)   Any provision of this subchapter which becomes effective by
declaration of the Street Commissioner or upon occurrence of certain weather
conditions shall, while temporarily in effect, take precedence over other
conflicting provisions of law normally in effect. However, it shall not take
precedence over provisions of law relating to traffic accidents, emergency
travel, authorized emergency vehicles, or emergency traffic directions by a
police officer.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 5, § 3) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.18 ANNOUNCEMENT OF DECLARATION.
   (A)   The Street Commissioner, upon the recommendation of the Police
Department, shall cause each declaration made by him or her pursuant to this
schedule to be publicly announced by means of broadcasts with a normal
operating range covering the town, and he or she may cause the declaration to
be further announced in newspapers of general circulation when feasible.
   (B)   Each announcement shall describe the action taken by the Street
Commissioner, including the time it became or will become effective, and shall
specify the streets or areas affected. A parking prohibition declared by the
Street Commissioner shall go into effect when designated. For purposes of this
schedule, the radio station over which the broadcast will be announced will be
station WIRE, Lebanon, Indiana. The Street Commissioner shall make or cause to
be made a record of each time and date when any declaration is announced to the
public in accordance with this schedule.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 5, § 4)
§ 71.19 TERMINATION OF PARKING PROHIBITION.
   Whenever the Street Commissioner finds that some or all of the conditions
which give rise to a parking prohibition in effect pursuant to the provisions
of this schedule no longer exist, he or she may declare the prohibition
terminated, in whole or in part, in a manner proscribed by this schedule effect
immediately upon announcement.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 5, § 5)
§ 71.20 SIGNS TO MARK SNOW EMERGENCY ROUTES.
   (A)   On each street designated by this schedule as a snow emergency route,
the Street Commissioner shall cause to be posted appropriated special signs.
   (B)   These signs shall be distinctive and uniform in appearance and shall
be plainly readable to person traveling on the street or highway.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 5, § 6)
Cross-reference:
   Designation of snow routes, see
Ch. 74, Sched. V
§ 71.21 STALLED VEHICLE ON SNOW EMERGENCY ROUTE.
   (A)   Whenever a vehicle becomes stalled for any reason, whether or not in
violation of this schedule, on any part of a snow emergency route on which
there is a covering of snow, sleet, or ice, or on which there is a parking
prohibition in effect, the person operating the vehicle shall take immediate
action to have the vehicle towed or pushed off the roadway of the snow
emergency route, either into the first cross-street which is not a snow
emergency route, or onto the public space of a nearby driveway.
   (B)   No person shall abandon or leave his or her vehicle in the roadway of
a snow emergency route (regardless of whether he or she indicates by raising
the hood or otherwise that the vehicle is stalled), except for the purpose of
securing assistance during the actual time necessary to go to a nearby
telephone or to a nearby garage, gasoline station, or other place of assistance
and return without delay.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 5, § 7) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.22 REMOVAL AND IMPOUNDMENT OF VEHICLES.
   (A)   Members of the Police Department are authorized to remove or have
removed a vehicle from a street to the nearest garage or other place of safety,
or to a garage designated or maintained by the Police Department or otherwise
maintained by the town, under the following circumstances or conditions.
      (1)   The vehicle is parked on a part of a snow emergency route on which
parking prohibition is in effect.
      (2)   The vehicle is stalled on a part of a snow emergency route on which
there is a covering of snow, sleet, or ice or on which there is a parking
prohibition in effect and the person who was operating the vehicles does not
appear to be removing it in accordance with the provisions of §
71.21.
      (3)   The vehicle is parked in violation of any parking ordinance or
provision of law and is interfering or about to interfere with snow removal
operations.
   (B)   Whenever an officer removes or has removed a vehicle from a street as
authorized in this subchapter, and the officer knows or is able to ascertain
from the registration records in the vehicle the name and address of the owner
thereof, the officer shall immediately give or cause to be given notice in
writing to the owner of the fact of the removal, the reasons therefor, and of
the place to which the vehicle is stored in a public garage, a copy of the
notice shall be given to the proprietor of the garage.
   (C)   Whenever an officer removes or has removed a vehicle from a street
under this subchapter and does not know and is not able to ascertain the name
of the owner, or for any other reason is unable to give the notice to the owner
as provided in division (B) above, and in the event the vehicle is not returned
to the owner within a period of three days, then the officer shall immediately
send or cause to be sent a written report on the removal by mail to the Bureau
of Motor Vehicles whose duty it is to register motor vehicles, and shall file a
copy of the notice with the proprietor of any public garage in which the
vehicle may be stored. The notice shall include a complete description of the
vehicle, the date, time, and place from which it was removed, the reasons for
the removal, and the name of the garage or place where the vehicle is stored.
   (D)   It shall be the duty of the Police Department to keep a record of each
vehicle removed in accordance with this subchapter. The record shall include a
description of the vehicle, its license number, the date and time of its
location, the name and address of its owner and last known operator, if known,
its final disposition, and the parking violation involved.
   (E)   This subchapter shall be supplemental to any other provisions of law
granting members of the Police Department authority to remove vehicles.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 5, § 8)
§ 71.23 RECOVERY OF IMPOUNDED VEHICLES.
   (A)   No person shall recover any vehicle removed in accordance with §
71.22(A), except as provided herein. Before the owner or person in charge of
the vehicle shall be allowed to recover it from the place where it has been
placed or impounded, he or she shall the place present to a member of the
Police Department evidence of this identity and right to possession of the
vehicle; sign a receipt for its return; and pay the reasonable towing and
storage charge.
   (B)   If the vehicle is not recovered within 15 days, abandoned vehicle
regulations shall apply.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 5, § 9)
§ 71.24 CITATION ON VEHICLES IN VIOLATION.
   (A)   Whenever any motor vehicle without a driver is found parked or left in
violation of any provision of this subchapter, and is not removed and impounded
for in this subchapter, the officer finding the vehicle shall take its
registration number and any other information displayed on the vehicle which
may identify its user, and shall conspicuously affix a traffic summons.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 5, § 10)
   (B)   In any prosecution with regard to a vehicle parked or left in a place
or in a condition in violation of any provision of this subchapter, proof that
the particular vehicle described in the complaint was parked or left in
violation of a provision of this subchapter together with proof that the
defendant named in the complaint was at the time the registered owner of the
vehicle, shall constitute prima facie evidence that the defendant was the
person who parked of left the vehicle in violation of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 5, § 11)
§ 71.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Violations of §§
71.15 through
71.24 shall be subject to fines set forth by the Ordinance Violations Bureau.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 5, § 13) (Ord. 99-7, passed 5-4-1999)
CHAPTER 72: PARKING REGULATIONS
Section
   
72.01   Parallel parking
   
72.02   Designated parking
   
72.03   Sidewalk or alley parking
   
72.04   Disregard of parking signs
   
72.05   Presumption in reference to illegal parking
§ 72.01 PARALLEL PARKING.
   When parked on roadway with a curb, the right-hand wheels of a vehicle must
be within 12 inches of the curb and parallel to it. The exception to this
provision shall be motorcycles, which shall be parked with the rear wheel at
the curb.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 7) Penalty, see §
10.99
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see I.C. 9-21-16-7
§ 72.02 DESIGNATED PARKING.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm, or corporation to park a vehicle
at any point which has been designated for parking for the Town Marshal, the
Fire Department, or any other proper legal authority.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 8) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 72.03 SIDEWALK OR ALLEY PARKING.
   It shall be unlawful to park on any sidewalk or in any alley within the
limits of the town, or parking so as to block any sidewalk, alley, or driveway
within the limits of the town.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 9) (Ord. 91-2, passed - -) Penalty,
see §
10.99
§ 72.04 DISREGARD OF PARKING SIGNS.
   It shall be unlawful to disregard any no parking sign or park in a
designated no parking zone within the limits of the town.
(Prior Code, Title 2, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 10) (Ord. 91-2, passed - -) Penalty,
see §
10.99
§ 72.05 PRESUMPTION IN REFERENCE TO ILLEGAL PARKING.
   In any prosecution charging a violation of any law or regulation governing
the parking or standing of a vehicle, proof that the particular vehicle
described in the notice to appear was parked in violation of any such law or
regulation, together with proof that the defendant named in the complaint was
at the time of such violation, the registered owner of such vehicle, shall
constitute prima facie evidence that such registered owner was the person who
parked such vehicle at the time and place for the time during which such
violation occurred.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 13) (Ord. 99-6, passed 4-6-1999)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 73.01 SKATEBOARDS.
   (A)   For the safety of the citizens of the town and the business patrons,
the riding of skateboards will not be allowed in the business district.
   (B)   The business district of the town shall be described as follows:
      (1)   Mill Street to the north;
      (2)   Jefferson Street to the south;
      (3)   Darlington Street to the west; and
      (4)   Walnut Street to the east.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 5, Ch. 3, § 1) Penalty, see §
73.99
GOLF CARTS, ATVS, AND UTVS
§ 73.15 PURPOSE.
   The purpose of this subchapter is to establish a Golf Cart and UTV Ordinance
within the town to ensure the safety and the welfare of persons operating such
vehicles within the town.
(Ord. 2021-07, passed 9-7-2021)
§ 73.16 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions apply unless
the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ALL-TERRAIN VEHICLE (ATV). A four or six wheel vehicle with a straddle seat
and handlebars.
   DRIVER’S LICENSE. A valid license issued to operate a motor vehicle issued
by the state or any other state.
   FINANCIAL RESPONSIBILITY. Liability insurance coverage on a golf cart or UTV
in an amount not less than required by state law for a motor vehicle operated
on public roadways in the state.
   GOLF CART. A vehicle designed and manufactured for operation on a golf
course for sporting or recreational purposes and is not capable of exceeding
speeds of 25 mph.
   ROADWAYS. Includes all public streets, alleys, and roads.
   UTILITY VEHICLE (UTV). A four-, six-, or eight-wheel vehicle with a non-
straddle seat and without handlebars.
(Ord. 2021-07, passed 9-7-2021)
§ 73.17 MANNER OF OPERATION.
   No person shall operate a golf cart or utility vehicle (UTV) in the town,
except as hereinafter provided.
(Ord. 2021-07, passed 9-7-2021) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.18 PROHIBITIONS OF ATVS.
   This subchapter does not apply to ATVs, as defined herein, as those vehicles
are prohibited on town roadways. Nothing in this subchapter shall be construed
to permit ATVs to be operated on town roadways under any circumstances.
(Ord. 2021-07, passed 9-7-2021) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.19 COMPLIANCE WITH ALL LAWS REQUIRED.
   Any and all applicable state laws regarding motor vehicles shall be adhered
to, including the possession and use of alcoholic beverages and illegal drugs.
Should a conflict exist between the provisions in this subchapter and
applicable state law requirements, the more restrictive provision applies.
(Ord. 2021-07, passed 9-7-2021) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.20 PERMIT AND DOCUMENTATION REQUIRED.
   (A)   No golf cart or UTV shall be operated in the town unless a permit from
the Town Marshal or his or her appointee has been issued to the owner of the
golf cart or UTV. The permit received from the town must be with the golf cart
or UTV whenever it is operated upon town roadways. The permit is valid for one
calendar year from date of issuance and must be renewed annually. Prior to
issuance or renewal of permit, the golf cart or UTV shall be inspected by the
Town Marshal to ensure that the vehicle complies with the requirements set
forth by the town and the state. A permit may not be issued if, in the previous
12 months, the applicant was cited and convicted of violating any provision of
this subchapter or other applicable state law.
   (B)   Golf cart and UTV owners must complete a registration form, waiver of
liability form, and provide a copy of proof of liability insurance prior to the
golf cart or UTV being inspected. The completed forms and proof of insurance
will be maintained by the Town Clerk-Treasurer.
   (C)   Any person who operates a golf cart or UTV in the town without first
obtaining a proper permit or completing the required paperwork pursuant to this
section will be subject to all state laws in addition to being in violation of
this subchapter.
(Ord. 2021-07, passed 9-7-2021) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.21 STANDARD EQUIPMENT REGULATION.
   All golf carts and UTV shall be equipped with all equipment required by the
state, including the following:
   (A)   Adequate brakes capable of producing deceleration at 14 feet per
second on level ground at a speed of 20 mph;
   (B)   DOT approved slow moving vehicle signs mounted in an unobstructed
fashion to the rear of the golf cart or slow moving (less than 30 mph) UTV;
   (C)   A golf cart must present one of the following.
      (1)   The golf cart shall have a safety tag on a staff holder displaying
such flag at least five feet above the surface of the street.
      (2)   The golf cart shall display an SAE approved amber or amber/clear
flashing beacon, visible from 360 degrees, with a flash rate of not less than
80 fpm and a minimum candlepower of 75,000 that is activated whenever the
vehicle is on the roadway.
   (D)   The golf cart or UTV shall be equipped with a rear view mirror;
   (E)   Golf carts and UTVs shall be equipped with a manufacturer’s serial
number plate;
   (F)   Golf carts and UTVs shall have front and rear reflectors; and
   (G)   Golf carts and UTVs shall have a functioning rear brake light which is
visible from a distance of 500 feet.
(Ord. 2021-07, passed 9-7-2021) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.22 PROOF OF LIABILITY INSURANCE.
   As part of the permit process, the owner of the golf cart or UTV must
provide proof of liability insurance before a permit will be issued. The proof
of liability insurance must be kept with the golf cart or UTV whenever said
golf cart or UTV is in operation on town roadways. Proof of liability insurance
must be provided annually in order to renew the golf cart or UTV permit.
(Ord. 2021-07, passed 9-7-2021) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.23 STATE REGISTRATION REQUIREMENTS.
   Any UTV shall be appropriately registered and titled with the state as
required by state law.
(Ord. 2021-07, passed 9-7-2021) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.24 TIMES AND CONDITIONS OF OPERATION.
   Golf carts and UTVs may be operated during the following times.
   (A)   Golf carts and UTVs may be driven on the town roadways only from
sunrise to sunset unless the golf cart is equipped with two headlamps (one on
each side of the front) and two operating taillights with brake lights (one on
each side of the vehicle) which are visible from a distance of 500 feet or the
UTV is equipped with one headlamp and one taillight.
   (B)   Golf carts and UTVs are prohibited on roadways during inclement
weather when visibility is reduced or impaired by weather, smoke, fog, or other
conditions or at any other time there is insufficient visibility to clearly see
a person or vehicle at a distance of 500 feet.
(Ord. 2021-07, passed 9-7-2021) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.25 OPERATION REGULATIONS.
   The following regulations apply to the operation of a golf cart or UTV
within the town.
   (A)   Golf carts and UTVs will adhere to all traffic flow patterns and will
operate on the right side of the roadway.
   (B)   (1)   Operators of golf carts and UTVs will adhere to all rules of the
road applicable to motorized vehicles as set forth by the State Bureau of Motor
Vehicles. A golf cart of UTV may only be operated by persons who are:
         (a)   At least 18 years of age and possess a valid driver’s license in
the case of a UTV;
         (b)   At least 16 years of age and possess a valid driver’s license in
the case of a golf cart; and
         (c)   If the operator is over the age of 16 years old, does not have a
license, and qualifies for handicapped parking, he or she may operate a golf
cart on public roadways upon the submission of a certificate signed by a
licensed physician that the driver is capable and able to operate a motorized
golf cart on the roadways designated. The operator must have a certificate and
handicap parking tag in his or her possession while operating a golf cart.
      (2)   For the purpose of this division (B), the following definition
applies unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
         UNDERAGE OPERATORS. A person under the age of 18 years old in the case
of UTV, or a person under the age of 16 years old in the case of golf carts,
may not legally drive the applicable vehicle on any town roadways.
   (C)   All riders in the golf cart or UTV must remain seated at all times.
   (D)   (1)   The number of occupants in a golf cart or UTV shall be limited
to the number of adult persons for whom individual seating is installed and
provided on the golf cart or UTV.
      (2)   The operator and all occupants shall be seated and no part of the
body of the operator or occupant shall extend outside the perimeter of the golf
cart or UTV while the golf cart or UTV is in motion.
   (E)   Anyone under the age of 18 who is riding on a UTV shall wear a helmet
that meets the standards established by the United States Department of
Transportation under 49 C.F.R. § 571.218 as in effect January 1,1979 in
accordance with I.C. 9-18.1-14-11.
   (F)   Children in golf carts or UTVs must be seated and not held. Children
three years and under must be in an approved car seat that is properly secured.
   (G)   Operators of golf carts or UTVs must indicate and signal intention to
turn either using vehicle-equipped turn signal system or by using appropriate
hand signals.
(Ord. 2021-07, passed 9-7-2021) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.26 SIDEWALKS AND ADJACENT AREAS.
   (A)   No golf cart or UTV shall be operated upon the public sidewalk, nor
shall they be operated upon that portion of the street located between the curb
line and the sidewalk or property line referred to as the “parking lane,”
except for the purposes of crossing the same to a public street at 90 degrees
which is authorized by this subchapter and Indiana Code.
   (B)   A total of two golf carts or UTV may use one parking space, provided
they are both able to park within the parking space lines.
(Ord. 2021-07, passed 9-7-2021) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.27 UNLAWFUL AND CARELESS OPERATION.
   (A)   No person shall operate a golf cart or UTV in a careless, reckless, or
negligent manner so as to endanger the person or property of another or to
cause injury or damage thereto.
   (B)   No person shall operate a golf cart or UTV in excess of the posted
speed limit of town roadway.
(Ord. 2021-07, passed 9-7-2021) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.28 TRESPASSING ON PRIVATE PROPERTY.
   Golf carts and UTVs shall not be operated on any private or town-owned
property without the permission and written consent of the property owner or
manager.
(Ord. 2021-07, passed 9-7-2021) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.29 EXCEPTIONS.
   All town employees are exempt from the above rules and regulations when
using a golf cart or UTV for town business. However, all town employees shall
at all times operate the golf cart or UTV in a safe manner and shall be subject
to all applicable state laws and the requirements in §
73.26. Exceptions may be made to the rules and regulations contained herein at
the discretion of the Town Marshal during town parades, special events,
festivals, and emergencies.
(Ord. 2021-07, passed 9-7-2021)
§ 73.30 PERMITTED AND PROHIBITED ROADWAYS.
   (A)   Golf carts and UTVs may be operated on all town roadways, subject to
the restrictions contained herein.
   (B)   Golf carts and UTVs are prohibited on the following roadways except as
to cross said roadways in compliance with the Indiana Code:
      (1)   State Road 75 (Lebanon Street);
      (2)   State Road 234; and
      (3)   U.S. 136 (Main Street).
   (C)   Exceptions to division (B) above may be as follows, subject to the
approval of the Town Marshal:
      (1)   During times of emergency wherein traditional vehicles cannot
traverse roadways normally;
      (2)   During sanctioned town events which feature a parade or other
activity utilizing non- traditional vehicles; and
      (3)   For emergency, utility, or police personnel.
(Ord. 2021-07, passed 9-7-2021) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.31 TOWN LIABILITY.
   (A)   The town, Town Council, Town Clerk-Treasurer, Town Police Department,
Town Marshal, and all town employees will assume no liability after issuing of
said golf cart or UTV permit.
   (B)   The town cannot be held responsible for any operator actions while
operating the golf cart or UTB on town roadways, alleys, or properties.
   (C)   The town cannot be held responsible for any death, injury, property
damage, or other damage which may occur from operator error, equipment
malfunction, or manufacturer defect of the golf cart or UTV on any street,
roadway, alley, or property of the town.
(Ord. 2021-07, passed 9-7-2021)
§ 73.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Violations of §
73.01 will result in a fine as stated in the Ordinance Violations Bureau’s
fines; $25 first offense; $50 second; and $75 third offense.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 5, Ch. 3, § 1)
   (C)   (1)   Any act constituting a violation of §§
73.15 through
73.31 or a failure to comply with any of its requirements shall subject the
offender, upon conviction or admission, to a fine not to exceed $250. Each
violation witnessed of any provision of §§
73.15 through
73.31 is violated shall constitute a separate offense, and the offender will be
charged an additional $25 per day plus any applicable court costs. All fees
shall be made payable to the town and paid to the Town Clerk-Treasurer.
      (2)   Any underage operator found to be in violation of §§
73.15 through
73.31 may be remanded to the Boone County Juvenile Court.
(Ord. 2006-4, passed 3-7-2006; Ord. 2021-07, passed 9-7-2021)
CHAPTER 74: TRAFFIC AND PARKING SCHEDULES
Schedule
      
I.   One-way streets
      
II.   Parking prohibited
      
III.   Preferential streets and alleys
      
IV.   Snow emergencies
SCHEDULE I. ONE-WAY STREETS.
   Darlington Street shall be and is hereby designated as a one-way, southbound
street from its intersection with Main Street to its end at Jefferson Street.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 1) Penalty, see §
10.99
SCHEDULE II. PARKING PROHIBITED.
   (A)   (1)   There will be no parking on South Darlington Street between Main
Street and Jefferson Street in the town.
      (2)   Violation of this division (A) shall be an offense punishable by a
fine of not less than $1 and not more than $25.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 5)
   (B)   (1)   This division (B) does not apply to a person who drives a
vehicle that becomes disabled while on the paved, improved, or main traveled
part of a street in a manner and to the extent that it is impossible to avoid
stopping and temporarily leaving the disabled vehicle on the street.
      (2)   A person may not stop, park, or leave standing an attended or
unattended vehicle upon the paved or main traveled part of a street, except
that section of South High Street from the point where it narrows south to its
intersection with State Road 234.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 12)
   (C)   (1)   It shall be unlawful to park or leave standing any vehicles on
either side of South High Street from a point beginning at the alleyway between
105 and 121 South High Street and continuing south to the intersection of South
High Street with State Road 234.
      (2)   Violation of this division (C) shall be an offense punishable by a
fine of $25 for the first offense, $50 for the second offense, and, at the
third and any subsequent offenses, the Town Police Department has the
discretion to tow the vehicle at the owner’s expense and fine the offender $75.
Each day a violation of this division (C) exists shall constitute a separate
offense.
(Ord. 99-6, passed 4-6-1999; Ord. 2021-05, passed 11-2-2021)
SCHEDULE III. PREFERENTIAL STREETS AND ALLEYS.
   (A)   Right-of-way. The following streets are hereby declared to be
preferential streets over certain named intersecting streets and alleys. The
traffic thereon shall have the right-of-way over traffic on such named
intersecting streets and alleys.
      (1)   North Darlington Street is preferential over the following
intersecting streets and alleys:
         (a)   Columbia Street;
         (b)   Ash Street;
         (c)   Elm Street (east and west);
         (d)   Mill Street (east and west); and
         (e)   All alleys intersecting with North Darlington Street.
      (2)   Elm Street in preferential over the following intersecting streets
and alleys:
         (a)   Stockton Street;
         (b)   North High Street;
         (c)   North Cemetery Street; and
         (d)   All alleys intersecting with Elm Street.
      (3)   Mill Street is preferential over the following intersecting streets
and alleys:
         (a)   Stockton Street; and
         (b)   Second Street.
      (4)   Stockton Street is preferential over the following intersecting
streets and alleys:
         (a)   Brush Street;
         (b)   Oak Street; and
         (c)   All alleys intersecting with Stockton Street.
      (5)   North High Street is preferential over the following intersecting
streets and alleys:
         (a)   Brush Street (east and west);
         (b)   Oak Street;
         (c)   Mill Street (east and west); and
         (d)   All alleys intersecting with North High Street.
      (6)   Second Street is preferential over the following intersecting
streets and alleys:
         (a)   Jefferson Street traffic traveling east; and
         (b)   All alleys intersecting with Second Street.
      (7)   First Street is preferential over all intersecting alleys south of
U.S. 136.
      (8)   South Darlington Street is preferential over all alleys
intersecting with South Darlington Street.
      (9)   South High Street is preferential over the following intersecting
streets and alleys:
         (a)   Jefferson Street; and
         (b)   All alleys intersecting with South High Street.
      (10)   Walnut Street is preferential over the following intersecting
streets and alleys:
         (a)   Jefferson Street;
         (b)   Vine Street; and
         (c)   All alleys intersecting Walnut Street.
      (11)   Lowery Street is preferential over the following intersecting
streets and alleys:
         (a)   Walnut Street; and
         (b)   Hillview Drive.
      (12)   Jefferson Street is preferential over the following intersecting
streets and alleys:
         (a)   First Street;
         (b)   South Darlington Street; and
         (c)   All alleys intersecting with Jefferson Street.
      (13)   The alley running parallel to and north of U.S. 136 is
preferential over the one-way alley bordering the west boundary of the town
park.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 3, § 1)
   (B)   Intersection passage. All traffic approaching the named preferential
streets from such intersecting streets and alleys shall, before proceeding,
come to a complete stop and permit traffic on the preferential streets to pass
through the intersection.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 3, § 2)
   (C)   Penalty. Any person violating any of the provisions of this schedule
shall be fined in any sum not less than $1 and not more than $100.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 3, § 3)
(Ord. 2009-4, passed 6-2-2009)
SCHEDULE IV. SNOW EMERGENCIES.
   (A)   The following streets or portions of streets within the town are
designated as snow emergency routes:
      (1)   South High Street from State Road 234 to Main Street;
      (2)   North High Street from Main Street to Elm Street;
      (3)   North Darlington Street from Main Street to end of corporation
limits;
      (4)   Elm Street from Darlington Street to North Lebanon Street;
      (5)   Mill Street from North Second to Lebanon Street;
      (6)   West Jefferson Street from South Second Street to South High
Street;
      (7)   East Jefferson Street from South High Street to South Walnut
Street; and
      (8)   South Second Street from West Jefferson Street to West Main Street.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 5, § 12)
   (B)   Violations of this schedule shall be subject to fines set forth in the
Ordinance Violations Bureau.
(Prior Code, Title 7, Article 1, Ch. 5, § 13)
(Ord. 99-7, passed 5-4-1999; Ord. 2009-4, passed 6-2-2009)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 90.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions apply unless the
context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ABANDONED. Placed or left upon public property or upon the private property
of another without the express permission of the owner, custodian, or tenant of
the property or is unattended or uncared for.
   ANIMAL. A member of the animal kingdom, except humans, dead or alive,
domestic or not.
(I.C. 15-17-2-3)
   ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER (ACO). A person who is authorized to implement and
enforce county animal ordinances and state statutes and as defined in state
statutes and is a sworn law enforcement officer, as defined under state law.
   ANIMAL FIGHTING CONTEST. Any event or activity facilitated by a person or
persons in which animals engage in violent, aggressive, or otherwise harmful
conduct with another animal in a form that is not generally associated with the
species under normal circumstances.
   ANIMAL CARE FACILITY. An animal control center, an animal shelter, a humane
society, or another animal impounding facility that has as its purpose the
humane care and treatment of animals.
(I.C. 6-9-39-7)
   AT LARGE. Leaving or straying away from the land owned, rented, or leased by
the owner or custodian of the animal or not being kept in direct control of an
owner or possessor of the animal. AT LARGE does not include the use of a dog
under the supervision of a person to hunt, chase, or tree predatory animals or
game birds, or the use of a dog to control or protect livestock or in other
related agricultural activities.
   BEAT. An intentional or knowing act of applying unnecessary physical force
or contact in a manner which has as its main objective inducing pain,
inflicting harm, or causing discomfort in a manner that could not reasonably be
described as an appropriate means of discipline.
   BITE. A wound inflicted by an animal tooth causing a tear, puncture,
abrasion, or other marking on the skin in which blood is visible or the skin is
damaged.
   CAT. All domestic members of the feline family.
   CATTERY. Any place in which three cats or more are kept for the purpose of
breeding or boarding for financial compensation.
   COLONY. A group of one or more feral cats, whether unmanaged or managed.
   CUSTODIAN.
      (1)   A person who is in temporary direct control of an animal as
authorized by the owner of the animal or is a law enforcement officer acting
within his or her scope of duties to impound or possess an animal.
      (2)   This may include, but is not limited to, a veterinarian, an animal
grooming facility, a law enforcement officer, or animal control officer.
   CRUELTY. Any intentional or knowing act or omission whereby unnecessary or
unjustifiable pain, suffering, or death is caused, permitted, or allowed to
continue where there is reasonable remedy or relief.
   DIRECT CONTROL. Under the immediate physical restraint of the owner or
custodian of the animal or within the confines of land owned, rented, or leased
by the owner or custodian of the animal.
   DOG. All domestic members of the canine family.
   DOMESTIC. Generally and commonly known to live in or about the habitation of
humans.
   DOMESTIC ANIMAL. An animal kept as a pet or used for service, protection,
comfort, companionship, hobby, or similar purpose.
   FERAL CAT. Any cat that has no apparent owner or identification and is wild,
untamed, unsocialized, unmanageable, or unable to be approached or handled.
   HARBOR. Performing acts of providing care, shelter, protection, restraint,
refuge, food, or nourishment.
   HEALTH DEPARTMENT. The Boone County Health Department.
   HUMANE TRAP. A device or procedure to contain or dispose of an unwanted
animal, as permitted by law, in a way that provides minimal discomfort or
unnecessary pain to the animal.
   IMPOUNDMENT. The act of taking physical possession and control of an animal
by an animal control officer or other person whom is empowered to act by law
and transporting it to an animal care facility or humane society.
   KENNEL. Any place in which three dogs or more are kept for the purpose of
breeding or boarding for financial compensation.
   LAW ENFORCEMENT OFFICER. An appointed officer or employee hired by and on
the patrol of the state, or any of the state’s political subdivisions, as
defined under state law, who is granted lawful authority to enforce all or some
of the penal laws of the state, and who possesses, with respect to those laws,
the power to effect arrests for offenses committed in the officer’s or
employee’s presence.
   LIVESTOCK. Cattle, sheep, swine, goats, bison, horses, mules, poultry, or
other animals that are commonly associated with activities associated with
farming or food production.
(I.C. 15-17-2-47)
   MANAGED COLONY. A colony of feral cats that are registered with a humane
society or designee and is maintained by a colony caretaker using trap, neuter,
and return methodology.
   MUTILATE. An intentional or knowing act of applying unnecessary physical
force or contact in a manner which has as its main objective creating changes
to the physical appearance of the animal in a manner that could not reasonably
be described as an appropriate and common modification for the animal species
involved. Spaying or neutering, or any other procedure that changes an animal
does not constitute MUTILATION if the procedure is done in a certified facility
by a person certified to perform the procedure or is a common or accepted
practice in the industry specific to the animal.
   NEGLECT. An intentional or knowing act or omission whereby an animal is
deprived of adequate and reasonable food, water, shelter, exercise, air, or any
other resource commonly associated with the health and wellbeing of the
particular animal species involved.
   OFFICE. The Boone County Sheriff’s Office.
   OWNER. Any person who owns, harbors, keeps, feeds, maintains, or has lawful
possession of an animal; however, this shall not include a person hired or
acting as custodian of the animal.
   PERSON. Any individual, group of individuals, firm, association,
partnership, or corporation.
   QUARANTINE. A place or period of isolation as to prevent cross-
contamination, infection, or other hazardous events as determined by a law
enforcement officer, animal control officer, Health Department, the humane
society, or any other agent permitted by law.
   SECURE RESTRAINT. A structure or device that maintains physical control of
the animal; this can include, but is not limited to, a fence of adequate design
and strength, a tethering device which is securely attached to the animal at
one end and a fixed object at the other end, or a cage. An “invisible fence,” a
fence of inadequate design and strength, or other structures or devices that
cannot maintain physical control of the animal under normal circumstances are
not considered a SECURE RESTRAINT.
   SPAY/NEUTER. An operation done to a female or male animal to prevent the
conception of offspring.
   STRAY. Any animal that does not appear, upon reasonable inquiry, to have an
owner, or has escaped restraint and is running at large.
   VICIOUS.
      (1)   Known to bite, attack, or injure human beings, domestic animals,
companion animals, or livestock without provocation.
      (2)   No animal may be declared VICIOUS if a threat, injury, or damage
was sustained by a human being who, at the time, was committing a willful
trespass or other tort upon the premises occupied by the owner or keeper of the
animal or was teasing, tormenting, abusing, assaulting, or otherwise provoking
the animal, or has, in the past, been observed or reported to have teased,
tormented, abused, assaulted, or otherwise provoked the animal involved, or was
committing or attempting to commit a crime.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 1)
§ 90.02 JURISDICTION.
   (A)   The Boone County Board of Commissioners finds that the terms and
conditions of this chapter are in the best interests of all citizens and
animals of county. Therefore, this chapter shall be in full force and effect in
both the incorporated and unincorporated part of the county unless or until a
municipality within in the county adopts an ordinance prohibiting enforcement
of this chapter within the boundaries of the municipality.
   (B)   For purposes of this subchapter, if a municipality (city or town) has
reorganized with a township, pursuant to I.C. 36-1.5-1-1 et seq., the term
INCORPORATED means areas within the former city or town limits and any platted
subdivision.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 2A)
§ 90.03 BASIC RESPONSIBILITIES AND DUTIES OF ANIMAL OWNERS.
   (A)   Every owner of every domestic animal kept in the county, whether in
the care of the owner or a custodian, shall see that such animal:
      (1)   (a)   Is kept in a clean, sanitary, and healthy manner and is not
confined so as to be forced to stand, sit, or lie in its own excrement.
         (b)   The owner or custodian of the animal shall regularly and as
often as needed maintain all animal areas to prevent odor or health and
sanitation problems;
      (2)   Shall be provided with proper amounts of food that is nutritionally
appropriate for the species to maintain good health;
      (3)   Shall have fresh drinking water;
      (4)   Shall have ventilation and appropriate shelter from the elements;
      (5)   Is able to exercise and move about freely, as needed by the
species;
      (6)   Shall not be tethered by use of a choke or pronged collar nor by
any rope, chain, or cord directly attached to the animal’s neck in lieu of an
appropriate collar, nor by a leash less than 12 feet in length or of such
unreasonable weight as to prevent the animal from moving about freely;
      (7)   Is protected against abuse, cruelty, neglect, torment, overload,
overwork, or any other mistreatment;
      (8)   Is provided with reasonable, necessary medical care or attention
and maintains current on inoculations outlined by this chapter or by state law;
and/or
      (9)   Is maintained in compliance with all applicable federal, state, and
local laws and regulations regarding animal care and control.
   (B)   Any person who witnesses a violation of this section shall notify the
Animal Control Officer or local law enforcement within 24 hours.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 2B) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.04 CRUELTY, ABUSE, AND NEGLECT.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for a person to commit, or otherwise participate
in, acts of animal cruelty. ACTS OF CRUELTY shall include, but is not limited
to, the following:
      (1)   An act of maliciously killing, abusing, maiming, or disfiguring any
animal or willfully or maliciously administering poison to any animal or
exposing any poisonous substance with the intent that the poisonous substance
shall be taken and consumed by such animal (does not include the killing of
animals for the protection of persons or property);
      (2)   An act of overloading, torturing, tormenting, depriving an animal
of its necessary sustenance or shelter, beating, mutilating, killing, or
carrying an animal in or upon a vehicle in a cruel or inhumane manner;
      (3)   An act of failing to supply an animal with wholesome food and
water, keeping an animal in an enclosure without wholesome exercise and
ventilation, or abandoning any animal to die;
      (4)   An act of owning, possessing, keeping, or training an animal with
the intent that such animal shall be engaged in an animal fighting contest;
      (5)   Building, maintaining, making, or keeping a pit on premises owned
or occupied by the person for the purpose of an exhibition of an animal
fighting contest;
      (6)   Encouraging, instigating, promoting, or assisting in an exhibition
of an animal fighting contest; or
      (7)   Charging admission, being an assistant, or promoting in an
exhibition of an animal fighting contest.
   (B)   Any Animal Control Officer or other officer empowered to act by law
may impound any animal pursuant to or during an investigation under this
chapter.
   (C)   Nothing in this section shall prohibit hunting or fishing as permitted
by the law of the state and the rules and regulations of the state’s Department
of Natural Resources.
   (D)   Nothing in this section shall prohibit the use of commercially sold
poisons or humane traps for the control of rats, mice, groundhogs, moles, or
other similar rodents, raccoons, possums, or other pests, as long as the person
using the poisons uses reasonable care to ensure that neither domestic animals,
nor livestock, are exposed to the poisons.
   (E)   If the number of domestic animals being kept or harbored by an owner
or custodian jeopardizes the health or welfare of the animals, some or all of
the animals may be impounded, and the Animal Control Officer may pursue any
remedies provided under this chapter.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 2C) Penalty, see §
90.99
Cross-reference:
   Animals sacrifice, see §
90.13
   Injured animals, see §
90.16
§ 90.05 RESTRAINT OF ANIMALS.
   (A)   (1)   It shall be unlawful for any owner or possessor of any domestic
animal to allow such animal to run at large, whether wearing a collar and tags
or not, within any incorporated area of the county.
      (2)   Any and all such domestic animals found at large may be immediately
impounded by the Animal Control Officer or any law enforcement officer and the
officers may pursue the animal onto private property to effect capture of the
animal.
   (B)   It shall be the duty of every owner or custodian of any domestic
animal that typically resides within any incorporated area of the county to
ensure that the animal is kept under secure restraint and that reasonable care
and precautions are taken to prevent the animal from leaving the real property
limits of its owner or custodian and ensure that the animal cannot easily dig,
climb, jump, or otherwise escape the secure restraint.
   (C)   (1)   Chaining of a domestic dog is discouraged, but if it is done,
the following is required.
         (a)   All basic responsibilities and duties described in this chapter
are met at all times.
         (b)   The chain must be at least 12 feet in length, regardless of the
size of the dog.
         (c)   The chain must be not of a weight heavy enough to cause physical
damage to the dog’s neck or body.
         (d)   The chain must be able to move freely in all directions.
      (2)   These restrictions do not apply to owners and their animals that
are participating in sanctioned dog shows or similar events.
   (D)   The owner or custodian of any guard dog or watchdog must confine such
animal within a perimeter fence and meet the following conditions:
      (1)   The fence shall be sufficient to prevent the dog’s escape with all
points of ingress and egress securely locked at all times; and
      (2)   A beware of dog, or similar wordage, sign shall be conspicuously
displayed on each exterior side of the enclosure for each 50 feet of enclosure,
with a minimum of two, as well as a sign on each ingress or egress point to the
enclosure. Signs shall be a minimum of ten inches high and 14 inches wide.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 2D) Penalty, see §
90.99
Cross-reference:
   Leash and control, see §
90.35
§ 90.06 RESTRAINT OF FEMALE DOMESTIC ANIMALS IN ESTRUS.
   The owner or custodian of any female domestic animal in estrus (commonly
referred to as heat) shall confine the animal within a secure enclosure and in
such a manner as to prevent the animal from becoming a nuisance and to prevent
conception, except during planned breeding.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 2E) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.07 PERMANENT IDENTIFICATION OF A DOMESTIC ANIMAL REQUIRED.
   (A)   A person who owns a domestic animal which is six months or older which
permanently resides in the county with an owner whose legal address falls
within the county limits shall ensure that at all times the animal bears a
permanent means of identification such that the owner can be ascertained
accurately, quickly, and easily.
   (B)   The means of identifications required by this section shall be in
addition to any tags required to be worn by state law of other provisions of
this chapter, and shall be either by:
      (1)   A microchip implanted in the animal that bears a registered
identification number and can be read by a standard microchip scanner; or
      (2)   A permanent tag attached to a durable collar worn at all times by
the animal and the tag bears the owner’s current name, address, and telephone
number.
   (C)   The identifying chip or tag may only be removed by the animal’s owner,
custodian, or veterinarian acting on behalf of the owner, and can only be
temporarily removed for reasonably short periods of time for the ability to
maintain the animal’s health and hygiene.
   (D)   Each veterinarian or other person in the county who implants a
microchip shall make available upon request to the animal control officer the
names, addresses, and phone numbers of the owners(s) of the animal and the
corresponding microchip identification number. Such records shall be available
to the animal control officer without court order.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 2F) (Ord. passed 6-1-2019) Penalty,
see §
90.99
§ 90.08 VACCINATIONS AND PROOF OF VACCINATION.
   (A)   The owners of all domestic animals within the county must comply with
vaccination requirements as set forth in state law, local ordinance, and the
rules and regulations for the State Board of Health and the Boone County Health
Department.
   (B)   (1)   All dogs, cats, and ferrets three months of age and older must
be vaccinated against rabies.
      (2)   The rabies vaccination of a dog, cat, and ferret shall be
maintained by ongoing revaccination of the animal as follows.
      (1)   Ferrets shall be revaccinated within 12 months of the prior
vaccination.
      (2)   Dogs and cats that are vaccinated with a rabies vaccine whose label
recommends annual boosters shall be revaccinated within 12 months of the prior
vaccination.
      (3)   Dogs and cats that are vaccinated with a rabies vaccine whose label
recommends a booster one year later and triennially thereafter shall be
revaccinated within 12 months of the first vaccination and shall be
revaccinated within 36 months of each vaccination thereafter.
   (C)   The owner of the animal is responsible for procuring the vaccinations
required by this section.
   (D)   All dogs shall have a rabies vaccination tag securely affixed to their
collar or harness at all times and owners of dogs, cats, and ferrets must be
able to provide documentation of rabies vaccination within 24 hours of being
asked by the animal control officer or local law enforcement agency.
   (E)   Vaccinations records must be supplied by the owner to the animal
control officer upon request if the animal has bitten, or is suspected of
biting, a person or other domestic animal.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 2G) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.09 ABANDONMENT.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for a person to knowingly, intentionally, or
recklessly abandon a domestic animal or livestock as described by this chapter.
   (B)   A defense to this section may include an unforeseen medical emergency
of the owner or custodian of the animal. Colonies and feral cats are excluded
from this section.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 2H) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.10 VICIOUS ANIMALS.
   It shall be unlawful for a person to cause, permit, accompany, or be
responsible for the presence of any vicious animal on the streets or public
places of the county or allow the animal to run on the premises of another at
any time, unless, in addition to the other requirements of this chapter, the
animal is securely muzzled to effectively prevent it from biting any person or
other animal.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 2I) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.11 ANIMAL BITES AND QUARANTINE.
   (A)   In the event of human being bit by a domestic animal, the animal shall
be quarantined in conformity with state law and the rules and regulations of
the State Board of Health and the Health Department.
   (B)   Every incident involving a human being bit by an animal shall be
reported within 24 hours to a local healthcare establishment, a law enforcement
agency, or the animal control officer. It is the duty of the person bitten or
the person’s parent or guardian to make the report in conformance with 410
I.A.C. 1-2.5-80 as amended.
   (C)   If the animal involved is located and able to be detained, the animal
shall be quarantined as determined by the Health Department and state law.
   (D)   Law enforcement animals maintaining current certification are exempt
from this section.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 2J) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.12 PUBLIC NUISANCE ANIMALS.
   (A)   A PUBLIC NUISANCE ANIMAL shall mean and include, but is not limited
to, a domestic animal that:
      (1)   Is found at large (stray);
      (2)   Damages the property of anyone other than the owner;
      (3)   Is vicious;
      (4)   Attacks without provocation;
      (5)   Excessively makes disturbing noises, including, but not limited to,
continued and repeated howling, barking, whining, or other utterances causing
unreasonable disturbance or discomfort to neighbors or others in close
proximity to the premises where the animal is kept; or
      (6)   Is not being kept in conformity with county ordinances and
regulations pertaining to land, animals, and ownership.
   (B)   (1)   A public nuisance animal may be impounded by the animal control
officer, without a court order, and the owner or custodian of the animal cited
for a violation of this chapter.
      (2)   The animal may be returned to the owner upon proof of ownership,
proof of payment of damages (if any), and proof of reasonable attempts to
mitigate the cause of nuisance determination.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 2K) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.13 ANIMAL SACRIFICE.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for a person to engage in, participate in, assist
in, or perform animal sacrifice. No person shall own, keep, possess, or harbor
any animal with the purpose or intention of using such animal for animal
sacrifice.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for a person to knowingly sell, offer for sale,
give away, or transfer any animal to any person when he or she knows or
believes that person intends to use such animal for animal sacrifice.
   (C)   Nothing in this section shall prohibit hunting or fishing as permitted
by the law of the state and the rules and regulations of the State Department
of Natural Resources.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 2L) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.14 VEHICLES AND ANIMALS.
   (A)   (1)   A person who is in operation of a vehicle which causes injury or
death to a domestic animal shall immediately notify the animal’s owner, if
known, or the local law enforcement agency or animal control officer.
      (2)   The person must provide the location of the incident, a description
of the animal, and the condition of the animal. Such person is not required to
provide his or her name or identifying information (i.e., an address, as the
only purpose of this requirement is to aid the stricken animal and notify its
owner).
   (B)   A person who is in operation of a vehicle which causes injury or death
to a nondomestic animal shall immediately notify the local law enforcement
agency or animal control officer if any of the following exists.
      (1)   The collision leaves debris or carnage which constitutes a road
hazard.
      (2)   The collision causes damage to a secondary vehicle or injury to a
pedestrian.
      (3)   The collision causes damage to private property if the driver of
the involved vehicle does not have a contractual interest with the property.
   (C)   No animal shall be left unattended in a vehicle, whether on private or
public property, in which the conditions of the vehicle would constitute a
health hazard to the animal.
   (D)   No animal shall be transported in the trunk of a vehicle, a small
storage compartment of a vehicle (i.e., glove box), or in any other fashion
which restricts the animal from reasonable mobility and access to air during
transport.
   (E)   An animal in a vehicle involved in a motor vehicle collision should
be:
      (1)   Released to the owner or custodian of the animal if possible;
      (2)   Be held by the law enforcement agency and released to a person
named by the owner or the custodian of the animal if that person can be to the
scene in a reasonable time period; or
      (3)   Transported to an animal care facility for a temporary holding
period.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 2M) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.15 STRAY ANIMALS.
   (A)   A person who finds a stray animal should notify the local law
enforcement agency or the animal control officer within 24 hours.
   (B)   A person possessing the lost or stray animal must comply with all
rules and regulations of this chapter pertaining to humane care and treatment
of animals while the animal is in custody awaiting the return to the owner or
intervention of an animal care facility, the local law enforcement agency, or
the animal control officer.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 2N) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.16 INJURED ANIMALS.
   (A)   A person who discovers an injured domestic animal or accidentally
causes injury to a domestic animal shall immediately notify the animal’s owner,
if known, the local law enforcement agency, or the animal control officer.
   (B)   (1)   The person must provide the location of the incident, a
description of the animal, and the condition of the animal.
      (2)   Such person is not required to provide his or her name or
identifying information (i.e., an address, as the only purpose of this
requirement is to aid the stricken animal and notify its owner).
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 2O) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.17 DECEASED ANIMALS.
   (A)   A person finding a dead domestic animal, large undomesticated animal
that constitutes a road or biohazard, or the surviving offspring of either,
shall call the local law enforcement agency or the animal control officer
immediately.
   (B)   If the local law enforcement agency is called, the agency shall:
      (1)   Notify the animal control officer if foul play is suspected or the
death appears to be caused by factors other than an accident, such as a
vehicular collision, or natural causes if the animal is a domestic animal; or
      (2)   Contact the appropriate agency to properly dispose of the animal’s
remains (i.e., the County Highway Department).
   (C)   (1)   Any deceased animal located on private property must be disposed
of within 24 hours in accordance with state law, the policy and/or rules of the
State Board of Animal Health, or industry standards as the case may dictate.
      (2)   The property owner is responsible for the disposal even if a third
party was responsible for the death of the animal.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 2P) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.18 LIVESTOCK AND FOWL.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm, or corporation to keep, harbor,
or maintain any swine, hogs, cattle, sheep, horses, ponies, fowl, or other
livestock within the corporate limits of the town.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 3, § 1) (Ord. 96-2, passed 7-8-1996)
Penalty, see §
90.99
LICENSING OF DOGS
§ 90.30 TOWN LIMITS.
   All dogs kept, owned, or harbored within the town shall be licensed by the
owner thereof.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 2, § 1) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.31 CHARGE.
   The license fee for each dog and cat shall be $5 per license, with a maximum
of $15 per household. Upon receipt of the license fee, the Clerk-Treasurer
shall issue tag or tags to the owner, as appropriate.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 2, § 2) (Ord. 2015-9, passed 12-1-2015)
§ 90.32 REGISTER.
   The Clerk-Treasurer shall keep a register of said license and issue tags to
the owner, which shall be attached to a collar worn by the dog.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 2, § 3)
§ 90.33 RUNNING AT LARGE.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful to permit any dog to run at large within the town
limits, and the permitting of the same is hereby declared to be a nuisance.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 2, § 4)
   (B)   Any dog found to be running at large in violation of division (A)
above shall be taken into custody by authority of the town and disposed of in
accordance with rules established by the Town Council.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 2, § 6)
Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.34 NUISANCE.
   It shall be unlawful to permit any dog within the town limits to disturb the
peace and quiet of the immediate surrounding neighborhood by constant barking.
The permitting of the same is hereby declared to be a nuisance.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 2, § 5) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.35 LEASH AND CONTROL.
   In the event any dog is on the streets of the town, it shall be on a leash
and under control of its owner.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 2, § 7) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.36 MUZZLED DOGS.
   (A)   In the event any owner has a dog which has a practice of escaping from
his or her custody or biting people, he or she shall keep a muzzle on said dog
at all times.
   (B)   In the event any such muzzled dog is found running loose on the
streets, such dog shall be taken into custody and the owner notified. If such
dog is not claimed by the owner within three hours after being notified, said
dog shall be disposed in accordance with the terms of §
90.33(B).
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 2, § 8) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.37 CUSTODY OF ANIMALS.
   (A)   In the event there is a violation of §
90.33(A), the same may be prosecuted on affidavit filed by the complaining
party. Upon receiving such complaint, the Town Marshal is authorized to take
such dog into custody.
   (B)   The Town Marshal shall keep such dog in his or her custody until the
owner is notified and the actions there under are remedied by proper steps to
be including, but not limited to, the muzzling of said dog.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 2, § 9)
LICENSING OF CATS
§ 90.50 TOWN LIMITS.
   All cats within the town shall be licensed by the owner. The OWNER is
defined as anyone that keeps, harbors, or feeds a cat.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 2A, § 1) (Ord. 2003-1, passed 3-4-2003)
Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.51 CHARGE.
   The charge for said license shall be set by the Town Council annually. The
same to be paid on the effective date of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 2A, § 2) (Ord. 2003-1, passed 3-4-2003)
§ 90.52 REGISTER.
   The Clerk-Treasurer shall keep a register of said license and issue tags to
the owner, which shall be attached to a collar worn by the cat.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 2A, § 3) (Ord. 2003-1, passed 3-4-2003)
§ 90.53 RUNNING AT LARGE.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful to permit any cat to run at large within the town
limits, and the permitting of the same is hereby declared a nuisance.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 2A, § 4)
   (B)   Any cat found running at large in violation of division (A) above
shall be taken into custody by the authority of the town and disposed of in
accordance with the rules established by the Town Council.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 2A, § 5)
Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   (1)   The owner of a domestic animal found to be roaming at large or
stray may be fined $50 for the first offense and $100 for each subsequent
offense involving the same animal occurring within one year.
      (2)   The owner of any animal, or person in whose care an animal is
entrusted, or other individual found to be in violation of any provision of §§
90.01 through
90.17 relating to cruelty, abuse, mutilation, sacrifice, or willful neglect of
an animal may be fined up to $1,000 for each offense or animal.
      (3)   For any other violation of §§
90.01 through
90.17, the owner may be fined up to $100.
      (4)   In addition to any fines imposed, the owner may be responsible for
any and all court costs imposed and may be responsible to reimburse the county
for any and all legal costs associated with the enforcement proceeding.
      (5)   An animal control officer may enter private property and
investigate any violation of §§
90.01 through
90.17 and impound any animal where there is reasonable suspicion that the
animal is a public nuisance, or is subject to, or in danger of, cruelty, abuse,
or neglect.
      (6)   All violations of §§
90.01 through
90.17 or any action seeking enforcement by fine or injunction shall be filed
and prosecuted by the Boone County Attorney or his or her designee in the Boone
County Superior Court.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 3)
   (C)   Each day’s violation of the term of §
90.18 shall constitute a separate offense for which the violator may be fined
in any sum, not exceeding $50 for the first offense, $75 for the second
offense, and $100 for the third offense.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 3, § 2)
   (D)   In the event any person violates any provision of §§
90.30 through
90.37, he or she shall be fined not less than $10, nor more than $500.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 2, § 10)
   (E)   In the event any person violates any provisions of §§
90.50 through
90.53, he or she shall be fined $50 for the first offense, $75 for the second
offense, and $100 for the third offense.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 1, Ch. 2A, § 6)
(Ord. 96-2, passed 7-8-1996; Ord. 2003-1, passed 3-4-2003; Ord. 2009-7, passed
8-4-2009)
