additional time (if applicable).
(Prior Code, Title 2, Article 3, § C)
(Ord. 2020-09, passed 11-10-2020)
§ 150.46 VIOLATION FINES.
   (A)   Residential structures (primary and accessory structures).
      (1)   There is a pre-construction fine for beginning or completing
construction without obtaining a permit of two times the amount of the permit
fee.
      (2)   This is in addition to the cost of the permit fee itself.
   (B)   Commercial/industrial structures (primary and accessory structures).
There is a pre-construction fine for beginning or completing construction
without obtaining a permit of three times the amount of the permit fee. This is
in addition to the cost of the permit fee itself.
   (C)   Other fines. There is a variance fine if a variance from the BZA is
required because construction resulted in a dimensional violation and did not
occur per the approved site plan or development plan. This fine is five times
the amount of the permit fee for the permit that was issued. This is in
addition to the application fee for the variance itself.
(Prior Code, Title 2, Article 3, § E) (Ord. 2020-09, passed 11-10-2020)
§ 150.47 APPLICATION FOR APPEALS, CONDITIONAL USES FEE.
   (A)   Variance: $50;
   (B)   Amendment, change of master plan, zone classification, or change of
text: $150;
   (C)   Change in development plan which previously has been approved: $50;
   (D)   Unit development plan:
      (1)   Less than 20 acres: $300;
      (2)   Twenty to 100 acres: $300 plus $2 per acre over 19 acres; and
      (3)   Over 100 acres: $5 per acre.
   (E)   Conditional use:
      (1)   Service stations (includes car wash, auto service center, and the
like): $250;
      (2)   Apartments, condominiums, mobile home parks, cooperatives, any type
of multi-family housing, shopping center, plus enclosed industrial use plans:
$250; and
      (3)   Other than divisions (E)(1) and (E)(2) above: $100.
(Prior Code, Title 2, Article 3, § F) (Ord. 2020-09, passed 11-10-2020)
§ 150.48 APPLICATION FOR OVERALL PROVISIONAL AND RECORD PLATS FEES.
   (A)   Overall provisional plat: $100 plus $1 for each lot;
   (B)   Resubmitted overall: $100 plus $1 for each lot provisional plat (which
has previously been rejected); and
   (C)   Record plat: $100 for plat having less than ten lots; $50 plus $5 per
lot for having more than nine but less than 50 lots; $5 per lot for plat having
50 or more lots.
(Prior Code, Title 2, Article 3, § G) (Ord. 2020-09, passed 11-10-2020)
§ 150.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   If any person, firm, or corporation shall violate any of the
provisions of §§
150.01 through
150.18, or shall do any act prohibited therein, or shall fail to perform any
duty lawfully enjoined, within the time prescribed by the Building Inspector,
or shall fail, neglect, or refuse to obey any lawful order given by the
Building Inspector in connection with the provisions of §§
150.01 through
150.18 for each such violation, failure, refusal, such person, firm, or
corporation shall be fined in any sum not less than $25, nor more than $300.
Each day of such unlawful activity as is prohibited by the first sentence of
this division (B) shall constitute a separate offense.
(Prior Code, Title 2, Article 4, Ch. 1, § 19) (Ord. 97-3, passed 6-3-1997)
CHAPTER 151: STREETS AND SIDEWALKS
Section
   
151.01   Street signs
   
151.02   Address numbers
   
151.03   Burning on a paved street
   
151.04   Cutting into streets or alleys
   
151.05   Obstruction of alleys
 
   
151.99   Penalty
§ 151.01 STREET SIGNS.
   (A)   Content, size, and aesthetics.
      (1)   Street signs shall contain the fully recognized (legal) street name
(or approved abbreviations) and include all required suffixes and/or direction
letters/numbers.
      (2)   Letter/number size shall be a minimum of six inches for street
names and four inches for suffix or direction letters/numbers.
      (3)   Signs shall be sized to allow for the use of the letters/numbers
noted above.
      (4)   The shape, color, and background shall be such that signs are
legible from any corner of an intersection and be of reflective finish. All
signs shall be in accordance with all applicable federal, state, and local
standards.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 12, Ch. 1, § 1)
   (B)   Sign location and placement. Street name signs shall be posted at the
point where a street name changes and at each intersection. Signs shall have a
height of seven feet from the bottom edge of the sign to the adjacent grade.
Street name signs should be located on the street corner. However, factors such
as visibility or grade changes may affect street name locations.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 12, Ch. 1, § 2)
(Ord. 2003-2, passed 5-6-2003) Penalty, see §
151.99
§ 151.02 ADDRESS NUMBERS.
   (A)   Size and content.
      (1)   Address numbers shall be a minimum of three inches in height for
residential applications and four inches in height for business and commercial
application. In all cases, the address numbers shall be legible from the
nearest public right-of-way.
      (2)   Address numbers shall contain the fully recognized (legal) address
number assigned to the property, including unit letters or numbers.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 12, Ch. 2, § 1)
   (B)   Location and placement.
      (1)   Address numbers shall be posted such that the number may be readily
seen from the street or public right-of-way.
      (2)   Address numbers posted on a building shall be located near the main
entrance door.
      (3)   Where distances or other circumstances prevent an address from
being posted on the building, address numbers may be posted on a mailbox or
appropriate post placed in the public right-of-way near the driveway access to
the building.
      (4)   Unit identifiers shall be posted for each unit in a location, which
is easily identifiable.
      (5)   Buildings which abut alleyways used by a motor vehicle shall also
display address numbers such that the number is visible from the alley side of
the building.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 12, Ch. 2, § 2)
   (C)   Responsibility. It is the responsibility of the property owner in
possession of any dwelling or place of business to display the designated
street numbers for that property.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 12, Ch. 2, § 3)
(Ord. 2003-2, passed 5-6-2003) Penalty, see §
151.99
§ 151.03 BURNING ON A PAVED STREET.
   (A)   The burning of leaves and rubbish on the surface of any paved street
or alley shall be and the same is hereby prohibited and declared to be
unlawful.
(Prior Code, Title 6, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 1)
   (B)   The Street Commissioner and Town Marshal are hereby given authority to
enforce this section upon observing any violation hereof or written complaint
of any person.
(Prior Code, Title 6, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 2)
Penalty, see §
151.99
§ 151.04 CUTTING INTO STREETS OR ALLEYS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm, or corporation to cut into
or across, or to excavate in any street or alley in the town, for any purpose
without first obtaining a permit so to do from the Clerk-Treasurer of the town.
(Prior Code, Title 6, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 4)
   (B)   Any person, firm, or corporation desiring to obtain such permit shall
make a written application so to do and file the same with the Clerk-Treasurer,
by which application the application shall state therein when and where he,
she, or it intends to cut into or make any excavation in any such street or
alley and state his, hers, or its reasons for so doing, and deposit with the
Clerk-Treasurer a sum of money or furnish bond with sufficient surety to be
approved by the Clerk-Treasurer in such amount as shall be fixed by the Street
Commissioner as a guarantee that the applicant will restore the street or alley
to as good condition as the same may be before the making of such a cut or
excavation. Such amount shall equal $100 per square foot. After such
restoration shall be made, the deposit or bond shall be returned to the
applicant. In the event such restoration shall not be made within a reasonable
time to be determined by the Town Council, the restoration may be made by the
town, and the deposit applied to the expense or be recovered upon the bond. The
time limit to complete such restoration shall be 90 days.
(Prior Code, Title 6, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 5)
Penalty, see §
151.99
§ 151.05 OBSTRUCTION OF ALLEYS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm, or corporation to place or
deposit any article, including tin cans, old iron, lumber, ashes or cinders,
garbage, dead animals, or any other article in the traveled portion of any
public alley in the town.
(Prior Code, Title 6, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 6) Penalty, see §
151.99
§ 151.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   (1)   Any property owner who fails to abide by the provisions of §§
151.01 or
151.02 will be subject to a $25 fine.
      (2)   Subsequent violations of §§
151.01 or
151.02 shall be subject to additional fines of not less than $25 nor more than
$100. Each day a violation occurs or continues shall constitute a separate
offense.
(Prior Code, Title 3, Article 12, Ch. 2, § 3)
   (C)   Violation of any of the provisions of §
151.03 may be punished by a fine of no more than $100 for the first offense,
$150 for the second offense, and $200 for the third offense.
(Prior Code, Title 6, Article 1, Ch. 1, § 3)
(Ord. 2003-2, passed 5-6-2003; Ord. 2009-7, passed 8-4-2009)
Cross-reference:
   Ordinance Violations Bureau, see
Ch. 33
